or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the estimated value of recurring contracts of the same type of good or service to be awarded during the\u00a012\u00a0months following the initial contract award or the procuring entity\u2019s fiscal year.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In the case of procurement by lease, rental or hire purchase of goods or services, or procurement for which a total price is not specified, the basis for valuation shall be:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0in the case of a fixedterm contract:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the term of the contract is\u00a012\u00a0months or less, the total estimated maximum value for its duration; or\n\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the term of the contract exceeds\u00a012\u00a0months, the total estimated maximum value, including any estimated residual value;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the contract is for an indefinite period, the estimated monthly instalment multiplied by\u00a048; and\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where it is not certain whether the contract is to be a fixedterm contract, the basis for valuation under point\u00a0(b) shall be used.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0121\n\n\n\nGeneral exceptions\n\n\n\nSubject to the requirement that such measures are not applied in a manner that would constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between the Parties or a disguised restriction on international trade, nothing in this Chapter shall be construed as preventing a Party from imposing or enforcing measures:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0necessary to protect public morals, order or safety;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0necessary to protect human, animal or plant life or health;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0necessary to protect intellectual property; or\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0relating to goods or services of persons with disabilities, philanthropic institutions or prison labour.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0122\n\n\n\nGeneral principles\n\n\n\n\n\nNondiscrimination\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0With respect to any measure regarding covered procurement, each Party, including its procuring entities, shall unconditionally accord, to the goods and services of the other Party and to the suppliers of the other Party offering such goods or services, treatment no less favourable than the treatment the Party, including its procuring entities, accords to its own goods, services and locally established suppliers.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0With respect to any measure regarding covered procurement, a Party, including its procuring entities, shall not:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0treat a locally established supplier less favourably than another locally established supplier on the basis of the degree of foreign affiliation or ownership; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0discriminate against a locally established supplier on the basis that the goods or services offered by that supplier for a particular procurement are goods or services of the other Party.\n\n\n\nUse of Electronic Means\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0When conducting covered procurement by electronic means, a procuring entity shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that the procurement is conducted using information technology systems and software, including those related to authentication and encryption of information, that are generally available and interoperable with other generally available information technology systems and software; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0maintain mechanisms that ensure the integrity of requests for participation and tenders, including establishment of the time of receipt and the prevention of inappropriate access.\n\n\n\nConduct of Procurement\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall conduct covered procurement in a transparent and impartial manner that:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0is consistent with this Chapter, using methods such as open tendering, selective tendering, limited tendering and electronic auctions;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0avoids conflicts of interest; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0prevents corrupt practices.\n\n\n\nRules of Origin\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party shall not, for the purposes of covered procurement, apply rules of origin to goods or services imported from or supplied from the other Party that are different from the rules of origin the Party applies at the same time in the normal course of trade to imports or supplies of the same goods or services from the same Party.\n\n\n\nMeasures Not Specific to Procurement\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Paragraphs\u00a01\u00a0and\u00a02 shall not apply to: customs duties and charges of any kind imposed on, or in connection with, importation; the method of levying such duties and charges; other import regulations or formalities and measures affecting trade in services other than measures governing covered procurement.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0123\n\n\n\nInformation on the procurement system\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promptly publish any law, regulation, judicial decision, administrative ruling of general application, standard contract clause mandated by law or regulation and incorporated by reference in notices or tender documentation and procedure regarding covered procurement, and any modifications thereof, in an officially designated electronic or paper medium that is widely disseminated and remains readily accessible to the public; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0provide an explanation thereof to the other Party, on request.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Part\u00a01 of Annex IV lists:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the electronic or paper media in which each Party publishes the information described in paragraph\u00a01 of this Article;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the electronic or paper media in which each Party publishes the notices required by Article\u00a0124, Article 126(7) and\u00a0Article 133(2); and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the website address or addresses where each Party publishes its notices concerning awarded contracts pursuant to Article\u00a0133(2).\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall promptly notify the Cooperation Committee of any modification to the Party\u2019s information listed in Part\u00a01 of Annex IV. The Cooperation Committee shall regularly adopt decisions reflecting the modifications to Part\u00a01 of Annex IV.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0124\n\n\n\nNotices\n\n\n\nNotice of Intended Procurement\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For each covered procurement, a procuring entity shall publish a notice of intended procurement in the appropriate paper or electronic medium listed in Part\u00a02 of Annex IV, except in the circumstances described in Article\u00a0130. Such medium shall be widely disseminated and such notices shall remain readily accessible to the public, at least until expiration of the time period indicated in the notice. The notices shall, for procuring entities covered under Parts\u00a01, 2 or\u00a03 of Annex III, be accessible by electronic means free of charge through a single point of access, for at least any minimum period of time specified in Part\u00a02 of Annex IV.\n\n\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Except as otherwise provided for in this Chapter, each notice of intended procurement shall include:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the name and address of the procuring entity and other information necessary to contact the procuring entity and obtain all relevant documents relating to the procurement, and their cost and terms of payment, if any;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a description of the procurement, including the nature and the quantity of the goods or services to be procured or, where the quantity is not known, the estimated quantity;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0for recurring contracts, an estimate, if possible, of the timing of subsequent notices of intended procurement;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a description of any options;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the time frame for delivery of goods or services or the duration of the contract;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the procurement method that will be used and whether it will involve negotiation or electronic auction;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where applicable, the address and any final date for the submission of requests for participation in the procurement;\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the address and the final date for the submission of tenders;\n\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the language or languages in which tenders or requests for participation may be submitted, if they may be submitted in a language other than an official language of the Party of the procuring entity;\n\n\n\n(j)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a list and brief description of any conditions for participation of suppliers, including any requirements for specific documents or certifications to be provided by suppliers in connection therewith, unless such requirements are included in tender documentation that is made available to all interested suppliers at the same time as the notice of intended procurement; and\n\n\n\n\n\n(k)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where, pursuant to Article\u00a0126, a procuring entity intends to select a limited number of qualified suppliers to be invited to tender, the criteria that will be used to select them and, where applicable, any limitation on the number of suppliers that will be permitted to tender.\n\n\n\nSummary Notice\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For each case of intended procurement, a procuring entity shall publish a summary notice that is readily accessible, at the same time as the publication of the notice of intended procurement, in English or French. The summary notice shall contain at least the following information:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the subject matter of the procurement;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the final date for the submission of tenders or, where applicable, any final date for the submission of requests for participation in the procurement or for inclusion on a multiuse list; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the address from which documents relating to the procurement may be requested.\n\n\n\nNotice of Planned Procurement\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Procuring entities are encouraged to publish in the appropriate paper or electronic medium listed in Part\u00a02 of Annex IV, as early as possible in each fiscal year, a notice regarding their future procurement plans (hereinafter referred to as \u201cnotice of planned procurement\u201d). The notice of planned procurement should include the subject matter of the procurement and the planned date of the publication of the notice of intended procurement.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity covered under Part\u00a03 of Annex III may use a notice of planned procurement as a notice of intended procurement provided that the notice of planned procurement includes as much of the information referred to in paragraph\u00a02 of this Article as is available to the entity and a statement that interested suppliers should express their interest in the procurement to the procuring entity.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0125\n\n\n\nConditions for participation\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall limit any conditions for participation in a procurement to those that are essential to ensure that a supplier has the legal and financial capacities and the commercial and technical abilities to undertake the relevant procurement.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In establishing the conditions for participation, a procuring entity:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0shall not impose the condition that, in order for a supplier to participate in a procurement, the supplier has previously been awarded one or more contracts by a procuring entity of a Party;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0may require relevant prior experience where essential to meet the requirements of the procurement; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0shall not impose the condition that, in order for a supplier of a Party to participate in a procurement or be awarded a contract, the supplier has previously been awarded one or more contracts by a procuring entity of the other Party or that the supplier has prior experience in the territory of that Party, except when prior experience is essential to meet the requirements of the procurement.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In assessing whether a supplier satisfies the conditions for participation, a procuring entity shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0evaluate the financial capacity and the commercial and technical abilities of a supplier on the basis of that supplier\u2019s business activities both inside and outside the territory of the Party of the procuring entity; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0base its evaluation on the conditions that the procuring entity has specified in advance in notices or tender documentation.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where there is supporting evidence, a Party, including its procuring entities, may exclude a supplier on grounds such as:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0bankruptcy;\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0false declarations;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0significant or persistent deficiencies in performance of any substantive requirement or obligation under a prior contract or contracts;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0final judgments in respect of serious crimes or other serious offences;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0professional misconduct or acts or omissions that adversely reflect on the commercial integrity of the supplier; or\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0failure to pay taxes.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0126\n\n\n\nQualification of suppliers\n\n\n\nRegistration Systems and Qualification Procedures\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party, including its procuring entities, may maintain a supplier registration system under which interested suppliers are required to register and provide certain information.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall ensure that:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0its procuring entities make efforts to minimise differences in their qualification procedures; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where its procuring entities maintain registration systems, the entities make efforts to minimise differences in their registration systems.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party, including its procuring entities, shall not adopt or apply any registration system or qualification procedure with the purpose or the effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to the participation of suppliers of the other Party in its procurement.\n\n\n\nSelective Tendering\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a procuring entity intends to use selective tendering, the entity shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0include in the notice of intended procurement at least the information specified in Article\u00a0124(2) (a), (b), (f), (g), (j) and (k) and invite suppliers to submit a request for participation; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0provide, by the commencement of the time period for tendering, at least the information in Article\u00a0124(2) (c), (d), (e), (h) and (i) to the qualified suppliers that it notifies as specified in Article\u00a0128(3) (b).\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall allow all qualified suppliers to participate in a particular procurement, unless the procuring entity states in the notice of intended procurement any limitation on the number of suppliers that will be permitted to tender and the criteria for selecting the limited number of suppliers.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where the tender documentation is not made publicly available from the date of publication of the notice referred to in paragraph\u00a04, a procuring entity shall ensure that those documents are made available at the same time to all the qualified suppliers selected in accordance with paragraph\u00a05.\n\n\n\nMultiUse Lists\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity may maintain a multiuse list of suppliers, provided that a notice inviting interested suppliers to apply for inclusion on the list is:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0published annually; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where published by electronic means, made available continuously,\n\n\n\nin the appropriate medium listed in Part\u00a02 of Annex IV.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The notice provided for in paragraph\u00a07 shall include:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a description of the goods or services, or categories thereof, for which the list may be used;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the conditions for participation to be satisfied by suppliers for inclusion on the list and the methods that the procuring entity will use to verify that a supplier satisfies the conditions;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the name and address of the procuring entity and other information necessary to contact the entity and obtain all relevant documents relating to the list;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the period of validity of the list and the means for its renewal or termination, or where the period of validity is not provided, an indication of the method by which notice of the termination of use of the list will be given;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0an indication that the list may be used for procurement covered by this Chapter.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Notwithstanding paragraph\u00a07, where a multiuse list will be valid for three years or less, a procuring entity may publish the notice referred to in paragraph\u00a07 only once, at the beginning of the period of validity of the list, provided that the notice:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0states the period of validity and that further notices will not be published; and\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0is published by electronic means and is made available continuously during the period of its validity.\n\n\n\n10.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall allow suppliers to apply at any time for inclusion on a multiuse list and shall include on the list all qualified suppliers within a reasonably short time.\n\n\n\n11.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a supplier that is not included on a multiuse list submits a request for participation in a procurement based on a multiuse list and all required documents, within the time period provided for in Article\u00a0128(2), a procuring entity shall examine the request. The procuring entity shall not exclude the supplier from consideration in respect of the procurement on the grounds that the entity has insufficient time to examine the request, unless, in exceptional cases, due to the complexity of the procurement, the entity is not able to complete the examination of the request within the time period allowed for the submission of tenders.\n\n\n\nEntities covered under Part\u00a03 of Annex III\n\n\n\n12.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity covered under Part\u00a03 of Annex III may use a notice inviting suppliers to apply for inclusion on a multiuse list as a notice of intended procurement, provided that:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the notice is published in accordance with paragraph\u00a07 of this Article and includes the information required under paragraph\u00a08 of this Article, as much of the information required under Article\u00a0124(2) as is available and a statement that it constitutes a notice of intended procurement or that only the suppliers on the multiuse list will receive further notices of procurement covered by the multiuse list; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the entity promptly provides, to suppliers that have expressed an interest in a given procurement to the entity, sufficient information to permit them to assess their interest in the procurement, including all remaining information required in Article\u00a0124(2), to the extent such information is available.\n\n\n\n13.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity covered under Part\u00a03 of Annex III may allow a supplier that has applied for inclusion on a multiuse list in accordance with paragraph\u00a010 of this Article to tender in a given procurement, where there is sufficient time for the procuring entity to examine whether the supplier satisfies the conditions for participation.\n\n\n\nInformation on Procuring Entity Decisions\n\n\n\n14.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall promptly inform any supplier that submits a request for participation in a procurement or application for inclusion on a multiuse list of the procuring entity\u2019s decision with respect to the request or application.\n\n\n\n15.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a procuring entity rejects a supplier\u2019s request for participation in a procurement or application for inclusion on a multiuse list, ceases to recognise a supplier as qualified, or removes a supplier from a multiuse list, the entity shall promptly inform the supplier and, on request of the supplier, promptly provide the supplier with a written explanation of the reasons for its decision.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0127\n\n\n\nTechnical specifications and tender documentation\n\n\n\nTechnical Specifications\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall not prepare, adopt or apply any technical specification or prescribe any conformity assessment procedure with the purpose or the effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to international trade.\n\n\n\nThe technical specifications must allow equal access of suppliers and must not have the effect of creating unjustified obstacles to the opening of procurement markets to competition.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In prescribing the technical specifications for the goods or services being procured, a procuring entity shall, where appropriate:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0set out the technical specification in terms of performance and functional requirements, rather than design or descriptive characteristics; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0base the technical specification on international standards, where such exist; otherwise, on national technical regulations, recognised national standards or building codes.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where design or descriptive characteristics are used in the technical specifications, a procuring entity should indicate, where appropriate, that it will consider tenders of equivalent goods or services that demonstrably fulfil the requirements of the procurement by including words such as \u201cor equivalent\u201d in the tender documentation.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall not prescribe technical specifications that require or refer to a particular trademark or trade name, patent, copyright, design, type, specific origin, producer or supplier, unless there is no other sufficiently precise or intelligible way of describing the procurement requirements and provided that, in such cases, the entity includes words such as \u201cor equivalent\u201d in the tender documentation.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall not seek or accept, in a manner that would have the effect of precluding competition, advice that may be used in the preparation or adoption of any technical specification for a specific procurement from a person that may have a commercial interest in the procurement.\n\n\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For greater certainty, a Party, including its procuring entities, may, in accordance with this Article, prepare, adopt or apply technical specifications to promote the conservation of natural resources or protect the environment.\n\n\n\nTender Documentation\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall make available to suppliers tender documentation that includes all information necessary to permit suppliers to prepare and submit responsive tenders. Unless already provided in the notice of intended procurement, such documentation shall include a complete description of:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the procurement, including the nature and the quantity of the goods or services to be procured or, where the quantity is not known, the estimated quantity and any requirements to be fulfilled, including any technical specifications, conformity assessment certification, plans, drawings or instructional materials;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any conditions for participation of suppliers, including a list of information and documents that suppliers are required to submit in connection with the conditions for participation;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0all evaluation criteria the entity will apply in the awarding of the contract, and, except where price is the sole criterion, the relative importance of such criteria;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the procuring entity will conduct the procurement by electronic means, any authentication and encryption requirements or other requirements related to the submission of information by electronic means;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the procuring entity will hold an electronic auction, the rules, including identification of the elements of the tender related to the evaluation criteria, on which the auction will be conducted;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where there will be a public opening of tenders, the date, time and place for the opening and, where appropriate, the persons authorised to be present;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any other terms or conditions, including terms of payment and any limitation on the means by which tenders may be submitted, such as whether in paper format or by electronic means; and\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any dates for the delivery of goods or the supply of services.\n\n\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In establishing any date for the delivery of goods or the supply of services being procured, a procuring entity shall take into account such factors as the complexity of the procurement, the extent of subcontracting anticipated and the realistic time required for production, destocking and transport of goods from the point of supply or for supply of services.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The evaluation criteria set out in the notice of intended procurement or tender documentation may include, among others, price and other cost factors, quality, technical merit, environmental characteristics and terms of delivery.\n\n\n\n10.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall promptly:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0make available tender documentation to ensure that interested suppliers have sufficient time to submit responsive tenders;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0provide, on request, the tender documentation to any interested supplier; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0reply to any reasonable request for relevant information by any interested or participating supplier, provided that such information does not give that supplier an advantage over other suppliers.\n\n\n\nModifications\n\n\n\n11.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where, prior to the award of a contract, a procuring entity modifies the criteria or requirements set out in the notice of intended procurement or tender documentation provided to participating suppliers, or amends or reissues a notice or tender documentation, it shall transmit in writing all such modifications or amended or reissued notice or tender documentation:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0to all suppliers that are participating at the time of the modification, amendment or reissuance, where such suppliers are known to the entity, and in all other cases, in the same manner as the original information was made available; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0in adequate time to allow such suppliers to modify and resubmit amended tenders, as appropriate.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0128\n\n\n\nTime periods\n\n\n\nGeneral\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall, consistent with its own reasonable needs, provide sufficient time for suppliers to prepare and submit requests for participation and responsive tenders, taking into account such factors as:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the nature and complexity of the procurement;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the extent of subcontracting anticipated; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the time necessary for transmitting tenders by nonelectronic means from foreign as well as domestic points where electronic means are not used.\n\n\n\nSuch time periods, including any extension of the time periods, shall be the same for all interested or participating suppliers.\n\n\n\nDeadlines\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity that uses selective tendering shall establish that the final date for the submission of requests for participation shall not, in principle, be less than\u00a025\u00a0days from the date of publication of the notice of intended procurement. Where a state of urgency duly substantiated by the procuring entity renders this time period impracticable, the time period may be reduced to not less than\u00a0ten\u00a0days.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Except as provided for in paragraphs\u00a04, 5, 7 and\u00a08, a procuring entity shall establish that the final date for the submission of tenders shall not be less than\u00a040\u00a0days from the date on which:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0in the case of open tendering, the notice of intended procurement is published; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0in the case of selective tendering, the entity notifies suppliers that they will be invited to submit tenders, whether or not it uses a multiuse list.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity may reduce the time period for tendering established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 to not less than\u00a0ten\u00a0days where:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the procuring entity has published a notice of planned procurement as described in Article\u00a0124(4) at least\u00a040\u00a0days and not more than\u00a012\u00a0months in advance of the publication of the notice of intended procurement, and the notice of planned procurement contains:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a description of the procurement;\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the approximate final dates for the submission of tenders or requests for participation;\n\n\n(iii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a statement that interested suppliers should express their interest in the procurement to the procuring entity;\n\n\n(iv)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the address from which documents relating to the procurement may be obtained; and\n\n\n(v)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0as much of the information that is required for the notice of intended procurement under Article\u00a0124(2), as is available;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the procuring entity, for procurements of a recurring nature, indicates in an initial notice of intended procurement that subsequent notices will provide time periods for tendering based on this paragraph; or\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a state of urgency duly substantiated by the procuring entity renders the time period for tendering established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 impracticable.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity may reduce the time period for tendering established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 by seven days in each one of the following circumstances:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the notice of intended procurement is published by electronic means;\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0all the tender documentation is made available by electronic means from the date of the publication of the notice of intended procurement; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the entity accepts tenders by electronic means.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The use of the provisions of paragraph\u00a05, in conjunction with paragraph\u00a04, shall in no case result in the reduction of the time period for tendering established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 to less than\u00a0seven\u00a0days from the date on which the notice of intended procurement is published.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Notwithstanding any other provision in this Article, where a procuring entity purchases commercial goods or services, or any combination thereof, it may reduce the time period for tendering established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 to not less than\u00a013\u00a0days, provided that it publishes by electronic means, at the same time, both the notice of intended procurement and the tender documentation. In addition, where the entity accepts tenders for commercial goods or services by electronic means, it may reduce the time period established in accordance with paragraph\u00a03 to not less than\u00a0seven\u00a0days.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a procuring entity covered under Part\u00a03 of Annex III has selected all or a limited number of qualified suppliers, the time period for tendering may be fixed by mutual agreement between the procuring entity and the selected suppliers. In the absence of agreement, the period shall not be less than\u00a0seven\u00a0days.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0129\n\n\n\nNegotiation\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party may provide for its procuring entities to conduct negotiations:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the entity has indicated its intent to conduct negotiations in the notice of intended procurement required under Article\u00a0124(2); or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where it appears from the evaluation that no tender is obviously the most advantageous in terms of the specific evaluation criteria set out in the notice of intended procurement or tender documentation.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that any elimination of suppliers participating in negotiations is carried out in accordance with the evaluation criteria set out in the notice of intended procurement or tender documentation; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where negotiations are concluded, provide a common deadline for the remaining participating suppliers to submit any new or revised tenders.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0130\n\n\n\nLimited tendering\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Provided that it does not use this provision for the purpose of avoiding competition among suppliers or in a manner that discriminates against suppliers of the other Party or protects domestic suppliers, a procuring entity may use limited tendering and may choose not to apply Articles\u00a0124, 125, 126, 127 (paragraphs\u00a07 to\u00a011), 128, 129, 131 and\u00a0132 only under any of the following circumstances:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0provided that the requirements of the tender documentation are not substantially modified, where:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0no tenders were submitted or no suppliers requested participation;\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0no tenders that conform to the essential requirements of the tender documentation were submitted;\n\n\n(iii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0no suppliers satisfied the conditions for participation; or\n\n\n(iv)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the tenders submitted have been collusive;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the goods or services can be supplied only by a particular supplier and no reasonable alternative or substitute goods or services exist for any of the following reasons:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the requirement is for a work of art;\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the protection of patents, copyrights or other exclusive rights; or\n\n\n(iii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0due to an absence of competition for technical reasons;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0for additional deliveries by the original supplier of goods or services that were not included in the initial procurement where a change of supplier for such additional goods or services:\n\n\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0cannot be made for economic or technical reasons such as requirements of interchangeability or interoperability with existing equipment, software, services or installations procured under the initial procurement; and\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0would cause significant inconvenience or substantial duplication of costs for the procuring entity;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0insofar as is strictly necessary where, for reasons of extreme urgency brought about by events unforeseeable by the procuring entity, the goods or services could not be obtained in time using open tendering or selective tendering;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0for goods purchased on a commodity market;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where a procuring entity procures a prototype or a first good or service that is developed at its request in the course of, and for, a particular contract for research, experiment, study or original development. Original development of a first good or service may include limited production or supply in order to incorporate the results of field testing and to demonstrate that the good or service is suitable for production or supply in quantity to acceptable quality standards, but does not include quantity production or supply to establish commercial viability or to recover research and development costs;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0for purchases made under exceptionally advantageous conditions that only arise in the very short term in the case of unusual disposals such as those arising from liquidation, receivership or bankruptcy, but not for routine purchases from regular suppliers; or\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where a contract is awarded to a winner of a design contest provided that:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the contest has been organised in a manner that is consistent with the principles of this Chapter, in particular relating to the publication of a notice of intended procurement; and\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the participants are judged by an independent jury with a view to a design contract being awarded to a winner.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall prepare a report in writing on each contract awarded under paragraph\u00a01. The report shall include the name of the procuring entity, the value and kind of goods or services procured and a statement indicating the circumstances and conditions described in paragraph\u00a01 that justified the use of limited tendering.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0131\n\n\n\nElectronic auctions\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Procuring entities may use electronic auctions.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In open, limited or negotiated procedures, a procuring entity may decide that the award of a contract shall be preceded by an electronic auction when the contract specifications can be established with precision.\n\n\n\nThe electronic auction shall be based:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0solely on prices when the contract is awarded to the lowest price; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0on prices and/or on the new values of the features of the tenders indicated in the specification when the contract is awarded to the most advantageous tender.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity which decides to hold an electronic auction shall state that fact in the notice of intended procurement.\n\n\n\nThe specifications shall include, inter alia, the following details:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the features, the values for which will be the subject of electronic auction, provided that such features are quantifiable and can be expressed in figures or percentages;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any limits on the values which may be submitted, as they result from the specifications relating to the subject of the procurement;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the information which will be made available to tenderers in the course of the electronic auction and, where appropriate, when it will be made available to them;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the relevant information concerning the electronic auction process;\n\n\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the conditions under which the tenderers will be able to bid and, in particular, the minimum differences which will, where appropriate, be required when bidding;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the relevant information concerning the electronic equipment used and the arrangements and technical specifications for connection.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Before proceeding with an electronic auction, a procuring entity shall make a full initial evaluation of the tenders in accordance with the award criterion or criteria set and with the weighting fixed for them. All tenderers who have submitted admissible tenders shall be invited simultaneously by electronic means to submit new prices and/or new values; the invitation shall contain all relevant information concerning individual connection to the electronic equipment being used and shall state the date and time of the start of the electronic auction. The electronic auction may take place in a number of successive phases. The electronic auction may not start sooner than two working days after the date on which invitations are sent out.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0When the contract is to be awarded on the basis of the most advantageous tender, the invitation shall be accompanied by the outcome of a full evaluation of the relevant tenderer. The invitation shall also state the mathematical formula to be used in the electronic auction to determine automatic rerankings on the basis of the new prices and/or new values submitted. That formula shall incorporate the weighting of all the criteria fixed to determine the most advantageous tender, as indicated in the contract notice or in the specifications; for that purpose, any ranges shall, however, be reduced beforehand to a specified value.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Throughout each phase of an electronic auction the contracting authorities shall instantaneously communicate to all tenderers at least sufficient information to enable them to ascertain their relative rankings at any moment. They may also communicate other information concerning other prices or values submitted, provided that that is stated in the specifications. They may also at any time announce the number of participants in that phase of the auction. In no case, however, may they disclose the identities of the tenderers during any phase of an electronic auction.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall close an electronic auction in one or more of the following manners:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0by indicating in the invitation to take part in the auction the date and time fixed in advance;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0when it receives no more new prices or new values which meet the requirements concerning minimum differences, by stating in the invitation to take part in the auction the time which it will allow to elapse after receiving the last submission before it closes the electronic auction;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0when the number of phases in the auction, fixed in the invitation to take part in the auction, has been completed.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0When the procuring entity has decided to close an electronic auction in accordance with point\u00a0(c) of paragraph\u00a07, possibly in combination with the arrangements laid down in point (b) of that paragraph, the invitation to take part in the auction shall indicate the timetable for each phase of the auction.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0After closing an electronic auction a procuring entity shall award the contract in accordance with Article\u00a0132 on the basis of the results of the electronic auction.\n\n\n\n\n\n10.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Procuring entities may not have improper recourse to electronic auctions nor may they use them in such a way as to prevent, restrict or distort competition or to change the subject matter of the contract, as put up for tender in the published notice of intended procurement and defined in the specification.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0132\n\n\n\nTreatment of tenders and awarding of contracts\n\n\n\nTreatment of Tenders\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall receive, open and treat all tenders under procedures that guarantee the fairness and impartiality of the procurement process, and the confidentiality of tenders.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall not penalise any supplier whose tender is received after the time specified for receiving tenders if the delay is due solely to mishandling on the part of the procuring entity.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a procuring entity provides a supplier with an opportunity to correct unintentional errors of form between the opening of tenders and the awarding of the contract, the procuring entity shall provide the same opportunity to all participating suppliers.\n\n\n\nAwarding of Contracts\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0To be considered for an award, a tender shall be submitted in writing and shall, at the time of opening, comply with the essential requirements set out in the notices and tender documentation and be from a supplier that satisfies the conditions for participation.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Unless a procuring entity determines that it is not in the public interest to award a contract, the entity shall award the contract to the supplier that the entity has determined to be capable of fulfilling the terms of the contract and that, based solely on the evaluation criteria specified in the notices and tender documentation, has submitted:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the most advantageous tender; or\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where price is the sole criterion, the lowest price.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a procuring entity receives a tender with a price that is abnormally lower than the prices in other tenders submitted, it may verify with the supplier that it satisfies the conditions for participation and is capable of fulfilling the terms of the contract.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall not use options, cancel a procurement or modify awarded contracts in a manner that circumvents the obligations under this Chapter.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0133\n\n\n\nTransparency of procurement information\n\n\n\nInformation Provided to Suppliers\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A procuring entity shall promptly inform participating suppliers of the entity\u2019s contract award decisions and, at the request of a supplier, shall do so in writing. Subject to Article\u00a0134 (2) and (3), a procuring entity shall, on request, provide an unsuccessful supplier with an explanation of the reasons why the entity did not select its tender and the relative advantages of the successful supplier\u2019s tender.\n\n\n\nPublication of Award Information\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0No later than\u00a072\u00a0days after the award of each contract covered by this Chapter, a procuring entity shall publish a notice in the appropriate paper or electronic medium listed in Part\u00a02 of Annex\u00a0IV. Where the entity publishes the notice only in an electronic medium, the information shall remain readily accessible for a reasonable period of time. The notice shall include at least the following information:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a description of the goods or services procured;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the name and address of the procuring entity;\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the name and address of the successful supplier;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the value of the successful tender or the highest and lowest offers taken into account in the award of the contract;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the date of award; and\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the type of procurement method used, and in cases where limited tendering was used in accordance with Article\u00a0130, a description of the circumstances justifying the use of limited tendering.\n\n\n\nMaintenance of Documentation, Reports and Electronic Traceability\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each procuring entity shall, for a period of at least three\u00a0years from the date it awards a contract, maintain:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the documentation and reports of tendering procedures and contract awards relating to covered procurement, including the reports required under Article\u00a0130; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0data that ensure the appropriate traceability of the conduct of covered procurement by electronic means.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0134\n\n\n\nDisclosure of information\n\n\n\nProvision of Information to Parties\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0On request of the other Party, a Party shall provide promptly any information necessary to determine whether a procurement was conducted fairly, impartially and in accordance with this Chapter, including information on the characteristics and relative advantages of the successful tender. In cases where release of the information would prejudice competition in future tenders, the Party that receives the information shall not disclose it to any supplier, except after consulting with, and obtaining the agreement of, the Party that provided the information.\n\n\n\nNonDisclosure of Information\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Notwithstanding any other provision of this Chapter, a Party, including its procuring entities, shall not provide to any particular supplier information that might prejudice fair competition between suppliers.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed as requiring a Party, including its procuring entities, authorities and review bodies, to disclose confidential information where disclosure:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0would impede law enforcement;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0might prejudice fair competition between suppliers;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0would prejudice the legitimate commercial interests of particular persons, including the protection of intellectual property; or\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0would otherwise be contrary to the public interest.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0135\n\n\n\nDomestic review procedures\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall provide a timely, effective, transparent and nondiscriminatory administrative or judicial review procedure through which a supplier may, in the context of a covered procurement, in which that supplier has, or has had, an interest, challenge:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a breach of this Chapter; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where the supplier does not have a right to challenge directly a breach of this Chapter under the domestic law of a Party, a failure to comply with a Party\u2019s measures implementing this Chapter.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The procedural rules for all challenges pursuant to paragraph\u00a01 shall be in writing and made generally available.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In the event of a complaint by a supplier, arising in the context of covered procurement in which the supplier has, or has had, an interest, that there has been a breach or a failure as referred to in paragraph\u00a01, the Party of the procuring entity conducting the procurement shall encourage the entity and the supplier to seek resolution of the complaint through consultations. The entity shall accord impartial and timely consideration to any such complaint in a manner that is not prejudicial to the supplier\u2019s participation in ongoing or future procurement or its right to seek corrective measures under the administrative or judicial review procedure.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each supplier shall be allowed a sufficient period of time to prepare and submit a challenge, which shall in no case be less than\u00a0ten\u00a0days from the time when the basis of the challenge became known or reasonably should have become known to the supplier.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall establish or designate at least one impartial administrative or judicial authority that is independent of its procuring entities to receive and review a challenge by a supplier arising in the context of a covered procurement.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where a body other than an authority referred to in paragraph\u00a05 initially reviews a challenge, the Party shall ensure that the supplier may appeal the initial decision to an impartial administrative or judicial authority that is independent of the procuring entity whose procurement is the subject of the challenge.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall ensure that a review body that is not a court shall have its decision subject to judicial review or have procedures that provide that:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the procuring entity shall respond in writing to the challenge and disclose all relevant documents to the review body;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the participants to the proceedings (hereinafter referred to as \u201cparticipants\u201d) shall have the right to be heard prior to a decision of the review body being made on the challenge;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the participants shall have the right to be represented and accompanied;\n\n\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the participants shall have access to all proceedings;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the participants shall have the right to request that the proceedings take place in public and that witnesses may be presented; and\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the review body shall make its decisions or recommendations in a timely fashion, in writing, and shall include an explanation of the basis for each decision or recommendation.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall adopt or maintain procedures that provide for:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0rapid interim measures to preserve the supplier\u2019s opportunity to participate in the procurement; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0where a review body has determined that there has been a breach or a failure as referred to in paragraph\u00a01, corrective action or compensation for the loss or damages suffered, which may be limited to either the costs for the preparation of the tender or the costs relating to the challenge, or both.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The rapid interim measures referred to in point (a) of paragraph\u00a08 may result in suspension of the procurement process. The procedures referred to in paragraph\u00a08 may provide that overriding adverse consequences for the interests concerned, including the public interest, may be taken into account when deciding whether such measures should be applied. Just cause for not acting shall be provided in writing.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0136\n\n\n\nModifications and rectifications to coverage\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party may propose a modification or rectification of the elements in Annex III which relate to that Party.\n\n\n\nModifications\n\n\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0When a Party proposes a modification, that Party shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0notify the other Party in writing; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0include in the notification a proposal for appropriate compensatory adjustments to the other Party to maintain a level of coverage comparable to that existing prior to the modification.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Notwithstanding point (b) of paragraph\u00a02, a Party need not provide compensatory adjustments if:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the modification in question is negligible in its effect; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the modification covers an entity over which the Party has effectively eliminated its control or influence.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The other Party shall be deemed to have accepted the modification, including for the purposes of Chapter\u00a014 (Dispute Settlement) of this Title, unless it objects in writing within\u00a045 days of receipt of the notification referred to in point (a) of paragraph\u00a02 that:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0an adjustment proposed under point (b) of paragraph\u00a02 is adequate to maintain a comparable level of mutually agreed coverage;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the modification is negligible in its effect under point (a) of paragraph\u00a03; or\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the modification covers an entity over which the Party has effectively eliminated its control or influence under point (b) of paragraph\u00a03.\n\n\n\nRectifications\n\n\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The following changes to Parts\u00a01 to\u00a03 of Annex III shall be considered a rectification, provided that they do not affect the mutually agreed coverage provided for in this Chapter:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a change in the name of an entity;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a merger of two or more entities listed within the same Part of Annex III; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the separation of an entity into two or more entities, provided that all new entities are added to the same Part of Annex III as the original entity.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Party proposing a rectification shall notify the other Party every two years, following the date on which this Title starts to apply.\n23\n\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party may notify the other Party of an objection to a proposed rectification within\u00a045 days from having received the notification referred to in paragraph\u00a06. Where a Party submits an objection, it shall set out the reasons why it believes the proposed rectification is not a change provided for in paragraph\u00a05, and describe the effect of the proposed rectification on the mutually agreed coverage provided for in this Agreement. If no such objection is submitted in writing within\u00a045 days after having received the notification, the Party shall be deemed to have agreed to the proposed rectification.\n\n\n\nThe Cooperation Committee\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If no objection is submitted regarding a proposed modification or rectification within the period provided for in paragraphs\u00a04 and\u00a07, the Cooperation Committee shall amend Annex III to reflect any such modification or rectification. The modification or rectification shall be effective from the day following the date of expiry of the period referred to in paragraphs\u00a04 and\u00a07.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If an objection to a proposed modification or rectification has been submitted, the Cooperation Committee shall discuss the matter. The Cooperation Committee may decide to approve a modification or rectification and amend Annex III accordingly.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0137\n\n\n\nTransitional period\n\n\n\n\n\nThis Chapter shall start to apply five years after the date on which this Title starts to apply. For the goods listed in Part\u00a04 of Annex III and for the services covered under Part\u00a06 of Annex\u00a0III, this Chapter shall start to apply eight years after the date on which this Title starts to apply.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a09\n\n\n\nRAW MATERIALS AND ENERGY\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0138\n\n\n\nDefinitions\n\n\n\nFor the purposes of this Chapter:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201craw materials\u201d means substances used in the manufacture of industrial products, excluding energy goods, processed fishery products or agricultural products, but including natural rubber, raw hides and skins, wood and wood pulp, silk, wool, cotton and other vegetable textile inputs;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cenergy goods\u201d means, based on the Harmonised Commodity Description and Coding System of the World Customs Organisation (HS) and the Combined Nomenclature of the European Union, natural gas, liquefied natural gas, liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) (HS\u00a027.11), electricity (HS\u00a027.16), crude oil and oil products (HS\u00a027.0927.10 and\u00a027.1327.15) and coal and other solid fuels (HS\u00a027.0127.04);\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cpartnership\u201d means any legal entity which is a commercial organisation under the jurisdiction or control of either Party such as, and not limited to, a corporation, trust, partnership, joint venture or association;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cservice supplier\u201d means a service supplier as defined in point (q) of Article\u00a040;\n\n\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cmeasure\u201d means a measure as defined in point (a) of Article\u00a040;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201ctransport\u201d means transmission and distribution of energy goods through the transmission pipelines for oil and oil products and highpressure natural gas, highvoltage electricity transmission grids and lines, railways, roadways and other facilities handling the transport of energy goods;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cunauthorised taking\u201d means any activity consisting of unlawful taking of energy goods from the transmission pipelines for oil and oil products and highpressure natural gas, highvoltage electricity transmission grids and lines, railways, roadways and other facilities handling the transport of energy goods;\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cemergency situation\u201d means a situation causing a significant disruption or a physical interruption of supply of natural gas, oil or electric energy between the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan, including supply transiting through third countries or a situation of an exceptionally high demand for energy goods within the European Union or the Republic of Kazakhstan in which market measures are not sufficient and nonmarket measures have to be additionally introduced;\n\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201clocal content requirement\u201d means:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0with respect to goods, a requirement for an enterprise to purchase or use goods of domestic origin or from a domestic source, whether specified in terms of particular products, in terms of volume or value of products, or in terms of a proportion of volume or value of its local production;\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0with respect to services, a requirement which restricts the choice of the service supplier or the service supplied to the detriment of services or service suppliers of the other Party;\n\n\n\n(j)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cstate owned enterprise\u201d means any enterprise involved in a commercial activity over which a Party at central or subcentral level directly or indirectly owns more than\u00a050\u00a0% of the enterprise\u2019s subscribed capital or of the votes attached to the shares issued by the enterprise;\n\n\n\n(k)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cjuridical person\u201d means a juridical person as defined in point (d) of Article\u00a040;\n\n\n\n(l)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cjuridical person of a Party\u201d means a juridical person of a Party as defined in point (e) of Article\u00a040.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0139\n\n\n\nPrice regulation\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties aim for the price of the supply of raw materials or energy goods for industrial users, if regulated by the government of a Party, to recover costs and provide for reasonable profit.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the price of raw materials or energy goods sold on the domestic market differs from the export price of the same product, the exporting Party shall, upon request of the other Party, provide information on such difference, excluding transportation costs and export taxes.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0140\n\n\n\nTrading and export monopolies\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall not maintain or establish a trading or export monopoly for raw materials or energy goods except when a Party exercises its priority (preemption) right to purchase raw and dry gas and gold.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0141\n\n\n\nAccess and rights to prospect, explore and produce hydrocarbons \n(crude oil and natural gas)\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Agreement shall affect the full sovereignty of the Parties in accordance with international law over hydrocarbon resources located in their territory and their inland, archipelagic and territorial waters, as well as sovereign rights for the purposes of exploring for and exploiting hydrocarbon resources located in their Exclusive Economic Zones and continental shelf.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties retain the right to determine the areas within their territory, inland, archipelagic and territorial waters, Exclusive Economic Zones and continental shelf to be made available for the exercise of the activities of prospecting, exploring for and producing hydrocarbons.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Whenever a sovereign decision of a Party, as described in paragraph\u00a02, is taken, each Party shall ensure that the enterprises of the other Party are not discriminated against as regards the access and exercise of the rights to prospect, explore for and produce hydrocarbons, provided the enterprise in question is established as a juridical person in the territory of the host Party granting the access.\n\n\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party may require an enterprise which has been granted an authorisation for the exercise of the activities of prospecting, exploring for and producing hydrocarbons, to pay a financial contribution or a contribution in hydrocarbons.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall take the necessary measures to ensure that licences or other authorisations, through which an enterprise is entitled to exercise the rights to prospect, explore for and produce hydrocarbons, are granted following a published procedure or an invitation to potentially interested applicants of the Parties to submit applications by means of a notice. The notice shall specify the type of licence or other authorisation, the relevant geographical area and the proposed date or time limit for granting a licence or other forms of authorisation.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Paragraphs\u00a03 to\u00a05 are without prejudice to the right of a state-owned enterprise to obtain access and rights to prospect, explore for and produce hydrocarbons by means of direct negotiations with its Party. When such a state-owned enterprise decides to transfer fully or partially its right to prospect, explore for and produce hydrocarbons, the obligations provided for in paragraphs\u00a03 and\u00a05 shall apply.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Article\u00a053 shall apply to the licensing conditions and the licensing authorisation procedure.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0142\n\n\n\nConditions for investment in raw materials and energy goods\n\n\n\nIn order to foster investment in the activities of prospecting, exploring for, extracting and mining of raw materials and energy goods, neither Party shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0maintain or adopt measures providing for local content requirements affecting the other Party\u2019s products, service suppliers, investors or investments unless otherwise provided for in the Protocol on the Accession of the Republic of Kazakhstan to the WTO and the GATS schedules of specific commitments of the European Union and its Member\u00a0States;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0maintain or adopt measures whereby an enterprise from the other Party is obliged to transfer or to share intellectual property rights in order to sell products or services or to invest on that Party\u2019s territory. The Parties are not precluded from negotiating contracts with investors seeking rights to prospect, explore for, extract and mine raw materials and energy goods for such transfers on a voluntary basis, provided that they are made under market conditions and at a market price.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0143\n\n\n\n\n\nTransit\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall take all necessary measures to facilitate the transit of energy goods, consistent with the principle of freedom of transit, and in accordance with Article\u00a07(1) and\u00a0(3) of the Energy Charter Treaty.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall prohibit the unauthorized taking of raw materials and energy goods transited or transported through its territory by any entity subject to its control or jurisdiction and shall take all appropriate measures to address such unauthorised taking.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0144\n\n\n\nInterruption\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall take all possible measures to ensure that operators of mainline energy transit or transport pipelines and grids:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0minimise the risk of accidental interruption, reduction or stoppage of transit and/or transport;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0expeditiously restore the normal operation of such transit or transport, which has been accidentally interrupted, reduced or stopped.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party through the territory of which the energy goods are in transit or transport, or in the territory of which they are in receipt and storage as part of the transport/transit route, shall not, in the event of a dispute over any matter involving the Parties or one or more entities subject to the control or the jurisdiction of a Party, interrupt or reduce, or permit any entity subject to its control or jurisdiction to interrupt or reduce, the existing transit, transport, receipt and storage as part of the transport/transit route of energy goods, except where this is specifically provided for in a contract or other agreement governing such transit, transport, receipt and storage as part of the transport/transit route, prior to the conclusion of a dispute resolution procedure under the relevant contract or the dispute settlement procedure set out in Chapter\u00a014 (Dispute Settlement) of this Title concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party shall not be held liable for an interruption or reduction pursuant to this Article in force majeure situations or where that Party is unable to supply energy goods or ensure their transit as a result of actions attributable to a third country or an entity under the control or the jurisdiction of a third country.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0145\n\n\n\nAccess to highvoltage electric energy transmission grids and lines\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall provide the enterprises of the other Party, established as juridical persons in the territory of the Party granting the access, with nondiscriminatory access to highvoltage electric energy transmission grids and lines, which are partly or fully owned and regulated by the Party granting the access within the available capacities of such grids and lines. The access shall be allocated in a fair and equitable manner.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0When applying measures relating to such transmission grids and lines, the Party shall ensure that the following principles are respected:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0all legal and regulatory measures on access and the transportation tariffs are fully transparent;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the measures do not discriminate with respect to the origin of the electricity production within its territory and with respect to the destination of the electricity; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0nondiscriminatory transportation tariffs with respect to enterprises of the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan are applied.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0146\n\n\n\nRegulatory authorities for electricity and gas\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall designate and empower regulatory authorities to regulate the markets for electricity and gas on its territory. Those regulatory authorities shall be legally distinct and functionally independent from any other public authorities or market participants.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The decisions of and the procedures used by a regulatory authority shall be impartial with respect to all market participants.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A market participant affected by any decision of a regulatory authority shall have the right to appeal against that decision to an appeal body. If the appeal body is not independent of the parties involved or is not judicial in character, the decisions of the appeal body shall be subject to a review by an impartial and independent judicial authority. The decisions of the appeal body and the judicial authority shall set out the reasons therefor and shall be in writing. The Parties shall ensure that the final decision of the appeal body or the judicial authority, whichever is the final instance, is enforced effectively.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0147\n\n\n\n\n\nRenewable energy sector\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0This Article shall apply to measures which may affect trade and investment between the Parties related to the generation of energy from renewable nonfossil sources, inter alia, wind, solar power and hydropower, but not to the products from which such energy is generated.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0refrain from maintaining or adopting measures requiring the formation of partnerships with local companies, unless such partnerships are deemed necessary for technical reasons and the Party maintaining or adopting such measures can demonstrate such technical reasons upon request by the other Party;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that any rules concerning authorisation, certification and licensing procedures, if applicable, in particular with regard to equipment, plants and associated transmission network infrastructures, are objective, transparent and nonarbitrary and do not discriminate against applicants from the other Party;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that administrative charges in renewable energy sector, such as those paid by consumers, planners, architects, builders, equipment installers and suppliers, are transparent and limited in amount to the approximate cost of services rendered;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that the importation and the use of goods originating in the other Party, or the provision of goods by the other Party\u2019s suppliers, are subject to the provisions of Chapter\u00a01 (Trade in Goods) of this Title;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that provision of services by the suppliers of the other Party are subject to Article\u00a053;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensure that the terms, conditions and procedures for the connection and access to electric energy transmission grids are transparent and do not discriminate against suppliers of the other Party or against electric energy from renewable sources. The Parties shall ensure that appropriate grid and marketrelated measures are taken to minimise the curtailment (limitations) of electric energy produced from renewable energy sources;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0refrain from imposing or maintaining a requirement for:\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0an enterprise of the other Party to purchase or use products of domestic origin or from any domestic source of the Party imposing the requirement, whether specified in terms of particular products, in terms of volume or value of products, or in terms of a proportion of volume or value of its local production; or\n\n\n(ii)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the enterprise\u2019s purchases or use of imported products to be limited to the amount related to the volume or value of local products that it exports.\n\n\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where international or regional standards exist with respect to equipment and systems for the generation of energy from renewable and nonfossil sources, the Parties shall use those standards, or their relevant parts, as a basis for their technical regulations except when such international standards or relevant parts would be an ineffective or inappropriate means for the fulfilment of the legitimate objectives pursued. For the purposes of applying this paragraph, the International Organization for Standardization (ISO) and the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC) shall be considered relevant international standardsetting bodies.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where appropriate, the Parties shall specify technical regulations based on product requirements in terms of performance, including environmental performance, rather than on product design or description.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Article shall be construed as preventing the adoption or enforcement by either Party of measures necessary for the safe operation of the energy networks concerned, or the safety of energy supply, subject to the requirement that such measures are not applied in a manner which would constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between the products, service suppliers or investors of the Parties where the same conditions prevail, or a disguised restriction on trade and investment between the Parties.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0148\n\n\n\nCooperation in raw materials and energy goods\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Without prejudice to Articles\u00a0204 to\u00a0208, the Parties agree to strengthen cooperation and the promotion of mutual understanding between them in the field of trade in raw materials and energy goods.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise that respecting the principles of transparency and nondiscrimination and ensuring that rules are not trade distortive is the best way to create an environment favourable to foreign direct investment in the production and trade of raw materials and energy goods. More generally, such an environment fosters the efficient allocation and efficient use of raw materials and energy goods.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Cooperation and the promotion of mutual understanding cover bilateral trade issues as well as issues of common interest stemming from international trade. Such issues include trade distortions impacting global markets, environment and development issues specifically linked to trade in raw materials and energy goods as well as corporate social responsibility in accordance with internationally recognized standards such as the OECD Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises and the OECD Due Diligence Guidance\u00a0for Responsible Supply Chains of Minerals from Conflict-Affected and High-Risk Areas. Cooperation and the promotion of mutual understanding include exchange of data and information on the regulatory framework of the raw materials and energy sectors. This shall not be construed as requiring the Parties to furnish any information, the disclosure of which they consider contrary to their respective security interests.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Either Party may request the organisation of an ad hoc meeting related to raw materials and energy goods or an ad hoc session on raw materials and energy goods during the Cooperation Committee meetings. The bilateral cooperation could additionally, if appropriate, be extended to the relevant plurilateral or multilateral fora in which both Parties participate.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0149\n\n\n\nEarly warning mechanism\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties establish an early warning mechanism to adopt practical measures aimed at preventing and rapidly reacting to an emergency situation or to a threat thereof.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall jointly undertake actions for:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0an early evaluation of potential risks and problems related to the supply and demand of natural gas, oil or electric energy; and\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the prevention or rapid reaction in case of an emergency situation or a threat thereof.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If either Party becomes aware of an emergency situation or of a situation which in its opinion could lead to an emergency situation, that Party shall notify the other Party within the shortest possible time.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For the purposes of this Article, the Parties agree that the responsible bodies are the Member of the European Commission in charge of energy and the Minister of the Republic of Kazakhstan in charge of the respective energy matters.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Upon notification, the Parties shall provide each other with an assessment of the situation.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Either Party may request consultations within three calendar days of the notification to:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0elaborate a common evaluation of the situation;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0develop recommendations to eliminate the emergency situation and to minimise the impact of the emergency situation;\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0create a Special Monitoring Group to, inter alia, monitor energy flows at the relevant points of the concerned infrastructure.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall, if appropriate, cooperate with third countries to eliminate the threat of an emergency situation or to overcome the emergency
