situation.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In case the emergency situation persists, either Party may start an emergency dispute settlement procedure, in accordance with the special mechanism provided for in Chapter\u00a014 (Dispute Settlement) of this Title.\n\n\n\n9.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall refrain from any actions that may deepen or reinforce the emergency situation, as appropriate in a given situation, from the moment of the notification.\n\n\n\n10.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party shall not rely on, or introduce as evidence in dispute settlement procedures under this Agreement, the following:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0positions taken or proposals made by the other Party in the course of a procedure under this Article; or\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any indication from the other Party of its willingness to accept a solution to the emergency situation referred to in this Article.\n\n\n\n11.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Cooperation Committee may develop, as necessary, detailed implementing provisions for the application of this Article.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0150\n\n\n\nExceptions\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0This Chapter is without prejudice to any exceptions, reservations or restrictions provided for in this Agreement.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0This Chapter shall not apply to research and development projects or to demonstration projects carried out on a noncommercial scale.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed as preventing the adoption or enforcement by either Party of measures necessary for the safe operation of the energy infrastructure, including energy transport and the production facilities concerned, in the interest of national security or public safety, including the prevention of and reaction to an emergency situation, subject to the requirement that such measures are not applied in a manner which would constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between the products, service suppliers or investors of the Parties where the same conditions prevail, or a disguised restriction on trade and investment between the Parties.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a010\n\n\n\nTRADE AND SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0151\n\n\n\nContext and objectives\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recall the Agenda\u00a021 of the United Nations Conference on Environment and Development of\u00a01992, the International Labour Organisation\u2019s (ILO) Declaration on Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work of\u00a01998, the Johannesburg Plan of Implementation on Sustainable Development of\u00a02002, the Ministerial Declaration of the UN Economic and Social Council on Generating Full and Productive Employment and Decent Work for All of\u00a02006, the ILO Declaration on Social Justice for a Fair Globalisation of\u00a02008 and the Outcome Document of the UN Conference on Sustainable Development of\u00a02012, incorporated in Resolution\u00a066/288 adopted by the UN General Assembly on\u00a027\u00a0July\u00a02012, entitled \u201cThe Future We Want\u201d.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties reaffirm their commitment to promote the development of international trade in such a way as to contribute to the objective of sustainable development, for the welfare of present and future generations. The Parties shall strive to ensure that this objective is integrated and reflected at every level of their trade relationship.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0152\n\n\n\nMultilateral environmental and labour standards and agreements\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise the value of international environmental governance and agreements as a response of the international community to global or regional environmental problems.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise that full and productive employment and decent work for all are key elements of sustainable development for all countries and a priority objective of international cooperation.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In that context, the Parties reaffirm their commitment to effectively implement in their law and practice the multilateral environmental agreements they are a party to and the ILO conventions ratified by the Member\u00a0States of the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan, respectively.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0153\n\n\n\nRight to regulate and levels of protection\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise the right of each Party to establish its own levels of domestic environmental and labour protection, and to adopt or modify its relevant law and policy accordingly, consistently with the internationally recognised standards and agreements referred to in Article\u00a0152. The Parties shall aim at high levels of environmental and labour protection.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise that it is inappropriate to encourage trade or investment by weakening or reducing the levels of protection afforded in domestic environmental or labour law.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party shall not derogate from or, through a sustained or recurring course of action or inaction, fail to effectively enforce its environmental and labour law, in order to encourage trade or investment.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0154\n\n\n\nTrade and investment promoting sustainable development\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties reaffirm their commitment to enhance the contribution of trade to the goal of sustainable development in its economic, social and environmental dimensions. Accordingly, they agree to promote:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0trade and investment in environmental goods and services and in climate-friendly products and technologies;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the use of sustainability assurance schemes, such as fair and ethical trade or ecolabelling; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0corporate social responsibility practices.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall exchange information on, and share experience in, their actions to promote coherence and mutual supportiveness between trade, social and environmental objectives. Furthermore, the Parties shall enhance their cooperation and dialogue on sustainable development issues that may arise in the context of their trade relations including on relevant aspects set out in Title IV (Cooperation in the Area of Economic and Sustainable Development).\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The cooperation and dialogue referred to in paragraph 2 of this Article shall involve relevant stakeholders, in particular social partners, as well as other civil society organisations, through the civil society cooperation established under Article\u00a0251.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Cooperation Committee may adopt rules for such cooperation and dialogue.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0155\n\n\n\nDispute Settlement\n\n\n\nSubsection\u00a02 of Section\u00a03 of Chapter\u00a014 (Dispute Settlement) of this Title does not apply to disputes under this Chapter. For any such dispute, after the arbitration panel has delivered its final report pursuant to Articles\u00a0180 and\u00a0182, the Parties, taking the report into account, shall discuss suitable measures to be implemented. The Cooperation Committee shall monitor the implementation of any such measures and shall keep the matter under review, including through the mechanism referred to in Article\u00a0154(3).\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a011\n\n\n\n\n\nCOMPETITION\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0156\n\n\n\nPrinciples\n\n\n\nThe Parties recognise the importance of free and undistorted competition in their trade relations. The Parties acknowledge that anticompetitive business practices and state interventions, including subsidies, have the potential to distort the proper functioning of markets and undermine the benefits of trade liberalisation.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0157\n\n\n\nAntitrust and mergers legislation and its implementation\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall maintain in its territory comprehensive competition law which effectively addresses anticompetitive agreements, concerted practices and anticompetitive unilateral conduct of enterprises with dominant market power, and which provides effective control of concentrations.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall maintain operationally independent authorities responsible and appropriately equipped for the effective enforcement of competition law as referred to in paragraph 1.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties recognise the importance of applying their respective competition law in a transparent and nondiscriminatory manner, respecting the principles of procedural fairness and rights of defence of the enterprises concerned.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0158\n\n\n\nState monopolies, state enterprises and enterprises entrusted \nwith special or exclusive rights or privileges\n\n\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Chapter prevents a Party from designating or maintaining state monopolies or state enterprises, or from entrusting enterprises with special or exclusive rights or privileges according to its law.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0With regard to state monopolies, state enterprises and enterprises entrusted with special or exclusive rights or privileges involved in economic activities, each Party shall ensure that such enterprises are subject to competition law as referred to in Article\u00a0157. For the purposes of this Chapter, an economic activity consists in offering goods and services on a market. It does not include activities performed in the exercise of governmental authority, namely activities carried out neither on a commercial basis nor in competition with one or more economic operators.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The application of competition law as referred to in Article\u00a0157 should not obstruct the performance, in law or in fact, of the particular tasks of public interest assigned to the enterprises in question. Exceptions should be limited and transparent. Trade and investment should not be affected to such an extent that would undermine the objective of this Agreement.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0159\n\n\n\nSubsidies\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For the purposes of this Article, a \u201csubsidy\u201d is a measure which fulfils the conditions of Article\u00a01 of the SCM Agreement, irrespective of whether it is granted to an enterprise for the production of goods or for the supply of services, and which is specific within the meaning of Article\u00a02 of that Agreement.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall ensure transparency in the area of subsidies. To that end, each Party shall report every two years from the date of application of this Title to the other Party on the legal basis, including the policy objective or the purpose of the subsidy, the duration or any other time limits, the form and, where possible, the amount or the budget and the recipient of the subsidy granted by its government or a public body. Such report is deemed to have been provided if the relevant information is made available on a publicly accessible website or through the WTO notification mechanism.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If a Party considers that a subsidy granted by the other Party is negatively affecting the first Party\u2019s interests, the first Party may request consultations on the matter. The requested Party shall accord due consideration to such a request. The consultations should, in particular, aim at specifying the policy objective of the subsidy, whether the subsidy has an incentive effect and is proportionate, and any measures taken to limit the potential distortive effect on trade and investment of the requesting Party\n24\n.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In order to facilitate the consultations, the requested Party shall provide information on the subsidy in question within a period no longer than\u00a090 days from the date of receipt of the request. If the requesting Party, after receiving information on the subsidy in question, considers that the subsidy in question negatively affects or may negatively affect the requesting Party\u2019s trade or investment interests in a disproportionate manner, the requested Party shall use its best endeavours to address the negative effects on the requesting Party\u2019s trade or investment interests caused by the subsidy in question.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Paragraphs\u00a03 and\u00a04 shall not apply to subsidies relating to fisheries and trade in goods covered by Annex\u00a01 to the WTO Agreement on Agriculture.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0160\n\n\n\n\n\nDispute settlement\n\n\n\nThe provisions of Chapter\u00a014 (Dispute Settlement) of this Title shall not apply with respect to Articles\u00a0156 to\u00a0158 and Article\u00a0159 (3) and (4).\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0161\n\n\n\nRelationship with the WTO\n\n\n\nThe provisions of this Chapter are without prejudice to the rights and obligations of a Party under the WTO Agreement, in particular the SCM Agreement and the Understanding on Rules and Procedures Governing the Settlement of Disputes.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0162\n\n\n\nConfidentiality\n\n\n\nWhen exchanging information under this Chapter, the Parties shall take into account the limitations imposed by the requirements of professional and business secrecy.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a012\n\n\n\nSTATEOWNED ENTERPRISES, \nSTATECONTROLLED ENTERPRISES \nAND ENTERPRISES GRANTED SPECIAL \nOR EXCLUSIVE RIGHTS OR PRIVILEGES\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0163\n\n\n\nDefinitions\n\n\n\nFor the purposes of this Chapter:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cstateowned enterprise\u201d means any enterprise involved in a commercial activity over which a Party at central or subcentral level owns more than\u00a050\u00a0% of the enterprise\u2019s subscribed capital or the votes attached to the shares issued by the enterprise;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cstatecontrolled enterprise\u201d means any enterprise involved in a commercial activity over which a Party at central or subcentral level exercises or has the possibility of exercising decisive influence, directly or indirectly, by virtue of its financial participation therein or by the rules or practices on its functioning, or by any other means relevant to establish such decisive influence. Decisive influence on the part of a Party shall be presumed when a Party, directly or indirectly, can appoint more than half of the members of the enterprise\u2019s administrative, managerial or supervisory body;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201centerprise granted special or exclusive rights or privileges\u201d means any enterprise, public or private, involved in a commercial activity, that has been granted by a Party, at central or subcentral level, in law or in fact, special or exclusive rights or privileges. Such rights or privileges may include the right to act as a distributor, a network provider or another intermediary for the purchase or sale of a good or for the provision or receipt of a service. \u201cEnterprises granted special or exclusive rights or privileges\u201d covers monopolies involved in a commercial activity;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0a \u201cmonopoly\u201d means an entity involved in a commercial activity, including a consortium, that in a relevant market in the territory of a Party is designated at central or subcentral level as the sole supplier or purchaser of a good or service, but does not include an entity that has been granted an exclusive intellectual property right solely by reason of such grant;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cspecial rights\u201d means rights granted by a Party at central or subcentral level to a limited number of enterprises within a given geographical area or a product or service market the effect of which is to substantially limit the ability of any other enterprise to carry out its activity in the same geographical area under substantially equivalent conditions. The granting of a licence or a permit to a limited number of enterprises in allocating a scarce resource through objective, proportional and nondiscriminatory criteria is not in and of itself a special right;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cnondiscriminatory treatment\u201d means national treatment or most-favoured-nation treatment as set out in this Agreement, whichever is better;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cin accordance with commercial considerations\u201d means consistent with customary business practices of a privately held enterprise operating according to market economy principles in international trade;\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u201cdesignate\u201d means to establish or authorise a monopoly, or to expand the scope of a monopoly, whether in law or in fact.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0164\n\n\n\n\n\nScope\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties confirm their rights and obligations under paragraphs\u00a01 to\u00a03 of Article XVII of the GATT\u00a01994, the Understanding on the Interpretation of Article XVII of the GATT\u00a01994, as well as under paragraphs\u00a01, 2 and\u00a05 of Article VIII of the GATS and the Chapter on Stateowned and Statecontrolled Enterprises and Enterprises with Special and Exclusive Privileges of the Protocol on the Accession of the Republic of Kazakhstan to the WTO, which are hereby incorporated into and made part of this Agreement and shall apply.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0This Chapter does not apply to covered procurement by a Party or its procuring entities within the meaning of Article\u00a0120.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0This Chapter shall apply to all economic activities covered by this Agreement. Services which are not listed in a Party\u2019s GATS schedule of specific commitments shall not be subject to the provisions of Articles\u00a0166 and\u00a0167.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0165\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Without prejudice to the Parties\u2019 rights and obligations under this Chapter, nothing in this Chapter prevents the Parties from establishing or maintaining stateowned or state-controlled enterprises or designating or maintaining monopolies or from granting enterprises special or exclusive rights or privileges.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where an enterprise falls within the scope of application of this Chapter, the Parties shall not require or encourage such an enterprise to act in a manner inconsistent with this Agreement.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0166\n\n\n\nNondiscrimination\n\n\n\nUnless otherwise provided for in Article\u00a0142 or in a Party\u2019s GATS schedule of specific commitments or in a Party\u2019s reservations to national treatment set out in Annex I, each Party shall ensure in its territory that any enterprise satisfying the conditions set out in points (c) and (d) of Article\u00a0163 in its purchase or sale of a good or a service accords nondiscriminatory treatment to a good of the other Party and/or to a service or a service supplier of the other Party.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0167\n\n\n\n\n\nCommercial considerations\n\n\n\nExcept to fulfil the purpose, such as a public service obligation, for which special or exclusive rights or privileges have been granted, or in the case of a stateowned or state-controlled enterprise to fulfil its public mandate, and provided that the enterprise\u2019s conduct in fulfilling that purpose or mandate is consistent with the provisions of Article\u00a0166 and Chapter 11 (Competition) of this Title, each Party shall ensure that any enterprise referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 acts in accordance with commercial considerations in the relevant territory in its purchases and sales of goods, including with regard to price, quality, availability, marketability, transportation and other terms and conditions of purchase or sale, as well as in its purchases or supply of services, including when those goods or services are supplied to or by an investment of an investor of the other Party.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0168\n\n\n\nPricing\n\n\n\nCharging different prices in different markets, or within the same market, where such differences are based on normal commercial considerations, such as supply and demand conditions, is not in itself inconsistent with\u00a0Articles 166 and\u00a0167.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0169\n\n\n\nCorporate governance\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall ensure that enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 observe high standards of transparency and corporate governance in accordance with the\u00a02005 OECD Guidelines on Corporate Governance of StateOwned Enterprises. Further development of the policy of corporate governance in enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 should be conducted in accordance with those Guidelines.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall ensure that any regulatory body responsible for regulating enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 is legally distinct and functionally independent from, and not accountable to, any of the enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall ensure the enforcement of laws and regulations in a consistent and nondiscriminatory manner at all levels of government, be it central or local, and including on enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163. Exemptions shall be limited and transparent.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0170\n\n\n\nExchange of information\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party which has a reason to believe that its interests under this Agreement are being adversely affected by the operations of an enterprise or enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 of the other Party, may request that latter Party to supply information about the operations of its enterprise relating to the carrying out of the provisions of this Agreement. Such information may include organisational, corporate and financial information.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall, at the request of the other Party, make available information concerning specific enterprises referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163 which do not qualify as small and mediumsized enterprises as defined in the law of the requested Party. Requests for such information shall indicate the enterprise, the products or services and markets concerned, and include indications that the enterprise is engaging in practices that hinder trade or investment between the Parties.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall, at the request of the other Party, make available information concerning exemptions, nonconforming measures, immunities and any other measures, including more favourable treatment, applicable in the territory of the requested Party to any enterprise referred to in points (a) to (d) of Article\u00a0163.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Paragraphs\u00a01 to\u00a03 shall not require any Party to disclose confidential information which would impede law enforcement or otherwise be contrary to the public interest or which would prejudice the legitimate commercial interests of particular enterprises.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a013\n\n\n\nTRANSPARENCY\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0171\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Each Party shall respond promptly to all requests by the other Party for specific information on any of its measures of general application or international agreements which pertain to or affect this Title. Each Party shall establish one or more enquiry points to provide to interested persons of the other Party, upon request, specific information on all such matters\n25\n. The Parties shall notify each other of the enquiry points within\u00a0three months of the date of application of this Title. Enquiry points need not be depositories of laws and regulations.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0All laws, regulations, decrees, decisions and administrative rulings of general application of the Parties pertaining to or affecting any matter governed by this Title shall be published promptly in a manner that fulfils the applicable requirements of the WTO Agreement, including those of Article X of the GATT\u00a01994, Article III of the GATS, and Article\u00a063 of the TRIPS Agreement. The Parties shall update published resources, including websites, containing such measures, on a regular basis and make them readily available to interested persons. Such measures shall be available while they are in effect and for a reasonable period after they are no longer in effect.\n\n\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall publish all laws, regulations, decrees, decisions and administrative rulings of general application pertaining to or affecting any matter governed by this Title, prior to their adoption. The Parties shall provide a reasonable period of time, normally not less than\u00a030 calendar days, for interested persons to comment to the responsible authorities before the relevant measure is finalised or submitted to the authorities responsible for its adoption. Any comments received during the period for comments will be taken into account.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0No law, regulation, decree, decision or administrative ruling of general application of the Parties pertaining to or affecting any matter governed by this Title shall become effective prior to publication.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Agreement shall require a Party to provide confidential information, the disclosure of which would impede law enforcement, or otherwise be contrary to the public interest, or which would prejudice legitimate commercial interests of particular enterprises, whether public or private.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Article\u00a055 shall apply with respect to this Chapter.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a014\n\n\n\nDISPUTE SETTLEMENT\n\n\n\n\nSECTION\u00a01\n\n\n\nOBJECTIVE AND SCOPE\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0172\n\n\n\nObjective\n\n\n\n\n\nThe objective of this Chapter is to establish an effective and efficient mechanism for avoiding and settling any dispute between the Parties concerning the interpretation and application of this Agreement with a view to arriving, where possible, at a mutually agreed solution.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0173\n\n\n\nScope of application\n\n\n\nThis Chapter shall apply with respect to any dispute concerning the interpretation and application of this Title , except as otherwise provided.\n\n\n\n\nSECTION\u00a02\n\n\n\nCONSULTATIONS AND MEDIATION\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0174\n\n\n\nConsultations\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall endeavour to resolve any dispute referred to in Article\u00a0173 by entering into consultations in good faith with the aim of reaching a mutually agreed solution.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0A Party shall seek consultations by means of a written request delivered to the other Party, copied to the Cooperation Committee, identifying the measure at issue and the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173 that it considers applicable.\n\n\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Party to which the request is made shall respond to the request for consultations within\u00a0ten days of the date of its receipt, unless otherwise provided for in this Agreement or agreed between the Parties.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The consultations shall be held within\u00a030 days of the date of receipt of the request and take place, unless the Parties agree otherwise, in the territory of the Party to which the request is made. The consultations shall be deemed concluded within\u00a030 days of the date of receipt of the request, unless both Parties agree to continue consultations. Consultations, and in particular all information disclosed and positions taken by the Parties during the consultations, shall be confidential, and without prejudice to the rights of either Party in any further proceedings.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Consultations on matters of urgency shall be deemed concluded within\u00a015 days of the date of receipt of the request by the requested Party unless both Parties agree to continue consultations.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the Party to which the request is made does not respond to the request for consultations within\u00a0ten days of the date of its receipt, or if consultations are not held within the timeframes laid down in paragraph\u00a03 or 4 of this Article, respectively, or if the Parties agree not to have consultations, or if consultations have been concluded and no mutually agreed solution has been reached, the Party that sought consultations may have recourse to Article\u00a0176.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0During consultations each Party shall provide sufficient factual information, so as to allow a complete examination of the manner in which the measure at issue could affect the operation and application of this Agreement.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The consultations shall be deemed concluded within five working days of the date of receipt of the request for consultations, unless the Parties agree otherwise, when they concern emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0175\n\n\n\nMediation\n\n\n\nAny Party may request the other Party to enter into a mediation procedure with respect to any measure adversely affecting trade or investment between the Parties pursuant to Annex VII.\n\n\n\nSECTION\u00a03\n\n\n\nDISPUTE SETTLEMENT PROCEDURES\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSUBSECTION\u00a01\n\n\n\nARBITRATION PROCEDURE\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0176\n\n\n\nInitiation of the arbitration procedure\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Where the Parties have failed to resolve the dispute by recourse to consultations as provided for in Article\u00a0174, the Party that sought consultations may request the establishment of an arbitration panel in accordance with this Article.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The request for the establishment of an arbitration panel shall be made by means of a written request delivered to the other Party and the Cooperation Committee. The complaining Party shall identify in its request the measure at issue, and it shall explain how such measure constitutes a breach of the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173 in a manner sufficient to present the legal basis for the complaint clearly.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0177\n\n\n\nEstablishment of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0An arbitration panel shall be composed of three arbitrators.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Within\u00a0ten days of the date of delivery, to the Party complained against, of the written request for the establishment of an arbitration panel, the Parties shall consult in order to reach an agreement on the composition of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In the event that the Parties are unable to agree on the composition of the arbitration panel within the time frame laid down in paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, each Party may, within\u00a0five days from the expiry of the timeframe established in paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, appoint an arbitrator from the sublist of that Party contained in the list established under Article\u00a0196. If either Party fails to appoint an arbitrator, the arbitrator shall, upon request of the other Party, be selected by lot by the chair of the Cooperation Committee, or the chair\u2019s delegate, from the sublist of that Party contained in the list established under Article\u00a0196.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Unless the Parties reach an agreement concerning the chairperson of the arbitration panel within the timeframe established in paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, the chair of the Cooperation Committee or the chair\u2019s delegate shall, upon request of either Party, select by lot the chairperson of the arbitration panel from the sublist of chairpersons contained in the list established under Article\u00a0196.\n\n\n\n5.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The chair of the Cooperation Committee, or the chair\u2019s delegate, shall select the arbitrators within five days of the request by either Party referred to in paragraph\u00a03 or 4.\n\n\n\n6.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The date of establishment of the arbitration panel shall be the last date on which all three selected arbitrators have accepted their appointment according to the Rules of Procedure set out in Annex V.\n\n\n\n7.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Should any of the lists provided for in Article\u00a0196 not be established or not contain sufficient names at the time a request is made pursuant to paragraph\u00a03 or 4 of this Article, the arbitrators shall be drawn by lot from the individuals who have been formally proposed by one or both of the Parties.\n\n\n\n8.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Unless the Parties agree otherwise, in respect of a dispute concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138 between the Parties, the second sentence of paragraph\u00a03 and paragraph\u00a04 of this Article shall apply without recourse to paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, and the period in paragraph\u00a05 of this Article shall be two days.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0178\n\n\n\nPreliminary ruling on urgency\n\n\n\nIf a Party so requests, the arbitration panel shall, within\u00a010 days of its establishment, give a preliminary ruling on whether it deems the case to be urgent.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0179\n\n\n\n\n\nConciliation for urgent energy disputes\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In respect of a dispute concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138 either Party may request the chairperson of the arbitration panel to act as conciliator concerning any matter related to the dispute by making a request to the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The conciliator shall seek an agreed resolution of the dispute or seek to agree a procedure to achieve such resolution. If within\u00a015 days of the date of his appointment the conciliator has failed to secure such agreement, he shall recommend a resolution to the dispute or a procedure to achieve such resolution and shall decide on the terms and conditions to be observed from a date which he shall specify until the dispute is resolved.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties and the entities under their control or jurisdiction shall respect recommendations made under paragraph\u00a02 on the terms and conditions for three months following the conciliator\u2019s decision or until resolution of the dispute, whichever is earlier.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The conciliator shall respect the Code of Conduct for Members of Arbitration Panels and Mediators (\u201cCode of Conduct\u201d) set out in Annex VI.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0180\n\n\n\nReports of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The arbitration panel shall deliver an interim report to the Parties setting out the findings of fact, the applicability of relevant provisions and the basic rationale behind any findings and recommendations that it makes.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Any Party may deliver a written request to the arbitration panel to review precise aspects of the interim report within\u00a014 days of its receipt.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0After considering any written comments by the Parties on the interim report, the arbitration panel may modify its interim report and make any further examination it considers appropriate.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The final report of the arbitration panel shall set out the findings of fact, the applicability of the relevant provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173 and the basic rationale behind any findings and conclusions that it makes. The final report shall include a sufficient discussion of the arguments made at the interim review stage, and shall answer clearly to the questions and observations of the Parties.\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0181\n\n\n\nInterim report of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The arbitration panel shall deliver an interim report to the Parties no later than\u00a090 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel. When the arbitration panel considers that this deadline cannot be met, the chairperson of the arbitration panel shall notify the Parties and the Cooperation Committee in writing, stating the reasons for the delay and the date on which the arbitration panel plans to deliver its interim report. Under no circumstances should the interim report be delivered later than\u00a0120 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In cases of urgency the arbitration panel shall make every effort to deliver its interim report within\u00a045 days and, in any case, no later than\u00a060 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel. Any Party may deliver a written request to the arbitration panel to review precise aspects of the interim report pursuant to Article\u00a0180(2) within\u00a0seven days of the delivery of the interim report.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In respect of a dispute concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138 between the Parties, the interim report shall be delivered\u00a0within 20 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel, and any request pursuant to Article\u00a0180(2) shall be delivered within five days of the delivery of the interim report. The arbitration panel may also decide to dispense with the interim report.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0182\n\n\n\nFinal report of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The arbitration panel shall deliver its final report to the Parties and to the Cooperation Committee within\u00a0120 days of the date of establishment of the arbitration panel. When the arbitration panel considers that this deadline cannot be met, the chairperson of the arbitration panel shall notify the Parties and the Cooperation Committee in writing, stating the reasons for the delay and the date on which the panel plans to deliver its final report. Under no circumstances should the final report be delivered later than\u00a0150 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In cases of urgency, the arbitration panel shall make every effort to deliver its report within\u00a060 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel. Under no circumstances should the final report be delivered later than\u00a075 days after the date of establishment of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In respect of a dispute concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138, the arbitration panel shall deliver its final report within\u00a040 days of the date of establishment of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nSUBSECTION\u00a02\n\n\n\nCOMPLIANCE\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0183\n\n\n\nCompliance with the final report of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\nThe Party complained against shall take the necessary measures to comply promptly and in good faith with the final report of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0184\n\n\n\nReasonable period of time for compliance\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If immediate compliance is not possible, the Parties shall endeavour to agree on the period of time to comply with the final report. In such a case, the Party complained against shall, no later than\u00a030 days after receipt of the final report of the arbitration panel, deliver a notification to the complaining Party and the Cooperation Committee of the time it will require for compliance (\u201cthe reasonable period of time\u201d).\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If there is disagreement between the Parties on the duration of the reasonable period of time, the complaining Party may, within\u00a020 days of receipt of the notification referred to in paragraph\u00a01 of this Article, request in writing that the arbitration panel established initially pursuant to Article\u00a0177 (\u201cthe original arbitration panel\u201d) determine the length of the reasonable period of time. Such request shall be delivered simultaneously to the other Party and to the Cooperation Committee. The arbitration panel shall deliver its report to the Parties and to the Cooperation Committee within\u00a020 days of the date of receipt of the request.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Party complained against shall notify the complaining Party in writing of its progress in complying with the final report of the arbitration panel. This notification shall be provided in writing and delivered at least one month before the expiry of the reasonable period of time.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The reasonable period of time may be extended by mutual agreement of the Parties.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0185\n\n\n\nReview of any measure taken to comply with the final report of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Party complained against shall notify the complaining Party and the Cooperation Committee of any measure that it has taken to comply with the final report of the arbitration panel. This notification shall be delivered before the end of the reasonable period of time.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In the event that there is disagreement between the Parties concerning the existence or the consistency of any measure notified under paragraph\u00a01 of this Article with the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173, the complaining Party may deliver a written request to the original arbitration panel to rule on the matter. Such request shall identify the specific measure at issue and explain how such measure is inconsistent with the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173, in a manner sufficient to present the legal basis for the complaint clearly. The arbitration panel shall deliver its report to the Parties and to the Cooperation Committee within\u00a045 days of the date of receipt of the request.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0186\n\n\n\nTemporary remedies in case of noncompliance\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the Party complained against fails to notify any measure taken to comply with the final report of the arbitration panel before the expiry of the reasonable period of time, or if the arbitration panel rules that no measure taken to comply exists or that the measure notified under Article\u00a0185(1) is inconsistent with that Party\u2019s obligations under the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173, the Party complained against shall, if so requested by the complaining Party and after consultations with that Party, present an offer for compensation.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the complaining Party decides not to request an offer for compensation under paragraph\u00a01 of this Article or, in case such request is made, if no agreement on compensation is reached within\u00a030 days of the date of expiry of the reasonable period of time or of the delivery of the arbitration panel report under Article\u00a0185(2), the complaining Party shall be entitled, upon notification to the other Party and to the Cooperation Committee, to take appropriate measures at a level equivalent to the nullification or impairment\n26\n caused by the violation. The notification shall specify such measures. The complaining Party may implement the measures at any moment after the expiry of\u00a0a ten-day period from the date of receipt of the notification by the Party complained against, unless the Party complained against has requested arbitration under paragraph\u00a03 of this Article.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the Party complained against considers that the appropriate measures are not at a level equivalent to the nullification or impairment caused by the violation of that Party\u2019s obligations under the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173, the Party complained against may deliver a written request to the original arbitration panel to rule on the matter. Such request shall be notified to the complaining Party and to the Cooperation Committee before the expiry of the\u00a0ten-day period referred to in paragraph\u00a02 of this Article. The original arbitration panel shall deliver its report on the measures notified by the complaining Party to the Parties and to the Cooperation Committee within\u00a030 days of the date of delivery of the request. The complaining Party shall not make the notified measures effective until the original arbitration panel has delivered its report. Such measure made effective after the delivery of the report shall be consistent with the arbitration panel report.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The measures made effective by the complaining Party and the compensation foreseen in this Article shall be temporary and shall not be applied after:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the Parties have reached a mutually agreed solution pursuant to Article\u00a0191; \n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the Parties have agreed that the measure notified under Article\u00a0185(1) brings the Party complained against in conformity with the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173; or\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0any measure that the arbitration panel under Article 185(2) has found to be inconsistent with the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173 has been withdrawn or amended so as to bring it in conformity with those provisions.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0187\n\n\n\nReview of any measure taken to comply \nafter the adoption of temporary remedies for noncompliance\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Party complained against shall notify the complaining Party and the Cooperation Committee of the measure it has taken to comply with the final report of the arbitration panel following the application of compensation or the taking of an appropriate measure by the complaining Party pursuant to Article\u00a0186, as the case may be. With the exception of cases under paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, the complaining party shall terminate the measure within\u00a030 days from receipt of the notification. In cases where compensation has been applied, and with the exception of cases under paragraph\u00a02 of this Article, the Party complained against may terminate the application of such compensation within\u00a030 days from receipt of the notification that it has complied with the final report of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0If the Parties do not reach an agreement on whether the Party complained against has complied with the final report of the arbitration panel within\u00a030 days from receipt of the notification under paragraph\u00a01 of this Article, the complaining Party shall deliver a written request to the original arbitration panel to rule on the matter. Such a request shall be delivered simultaneously to the other Party and to the Cooperation Committee. The arbitration panel report shall be delivered to the Parties and to the Cooperation Committee within\u00a045 days of the date of the submission of the request. If the arbitration panel rules that the Party complained against has complied with the final report of the arbitration panel, the complaining Party shall terminate the appropriate measure taken under Article\u00a0186 or the Party complained against shall terminate the compensation, as the case may be. If the arbitration panel rules that the Party complained against has not fully complied with the final report of the arbitration panel, the compensation or the appropriate measure taken pursuant to Article\u00a0186 shall be adapted in light of the arbitration panel report.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0188\n\n\n\nRemedies for urgent energy disputes\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In respect of a dispute concerning emergency situations as defined in point (h) of Article\u00a0138 between the Parties, this Article shall apply.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0By way of derogation from Articles\u00a0184, 185 and\u00a0186,\u00a0the complaining Party may take appropriate measures to a level equivalent to the nullification or impairment caused by a Party failing to bring itself into compliance with the final report of the arbitration panel within\u00a015 days of its release. Those measures may take effect immediately. Such measures may be maintained as long as the Party complained against has not complied with the final report of the arbitration panel.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Should the Party complained against dispute the existence of a failure to comply or the proportionality of the measure made effective by the complaining Party or its failure to comply, it may initiate proceedings under Article\u00a0186(3) and\u00a0Article 187 which shall be examined expeditiously. The complaining Party shall be required to remove or adjust the measures only once the arbitration panel has ruled on the matter, and may maintain the measures pending the proceedings.\n\n\n\nSUBSECTION\u00a03\n\n\n\nCOMMON PROVISIONS\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0189\n\n\n\nReplacement of arbitrators\n\n\n\nIf in an arbitration proceeding under this Chapter the original arbitration panel, or some of its members, are unable to participate, withdraw, or need to be replaced because they do not comply with the requirements of the Code of Conduct set out in Annex VI, the procedure set out in Article\u00a0177 shall apply. The time limit for the delivery of the report may be extended for the time necessary for the appointment of a new arbitrator but for no longer than\u00a020 days.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0190\n\n\n\nSuspension and termination of arbitration and compliance procedures\n\n\n\nThe arbitration panel shall, at the request of both Parties, suspend its work at any time for a period agreed by the Parties not exceeding\u00a012 consecutive months. The arbitration panel shall resume its work before the end of that period at the written request of both Parties or at the end of that period at the written request of either Party. The requesting Party shall notify the chair of the Cooperation Committee and the other Party accordingly. If a Party does not request the resumption of the arbitration panel\u2019s work at the expiry of the agreed suspension period, the procedure shall be terminated. The suspension and termination of the arbitration panel\u2019s work are without prejudice to the rights of either Party in other proceedings subject to Article\u00a0197.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0191\n\n\n\nMutually agreed solution\n\n\n\nThe Parties may reach a mutually agreed solution to a dispute under this Chapter at any time. They shall jointly notify the Cooperation Committee and the chairperson of the arbitration panel, where applicable, of any such solution. If the solution requires approval pursuant to the relevant domestic procedures of either Party, the notification shall refer to this requirement, and the dispute settlement procedure shall be suspended. If such approval is not required, or if the completion of any such domestic procedures is notified, the dispute settlement procedure shall be terminated.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0192\n\n\n\n\n\nRules of Procedure\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Dispute settlement procedures under this Chapter shall be governed by the Rules of Procedure set out in Annex V and by the Code of Conduct set out in Annex VI.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Any hearing of the arbitration panel shall be open to the public unless otherwise provided for in the Rules of Procedure set out in Annex V.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0193\n\n\n\nInformation and technical advice\n\n\n\nAt the request of a Party, or on its own initiative, the arbitration panel may request any information it deems appropriate for the arbitration panel proceedings from any source, including the Parties involved in the dispute. The arbitration panel also has the right to seek the opinion of experts, as it deems appropriate. The arbitration panel shall consult the Parties before choosing such experts. Natural or legal persons established in the territory of a Party may submit amicus curiae briefs to the arbitration panel in accordance with the Rules of Procedure set out in Annex V. Any information obtained under this Article shall be disclosed to each Party and submitted for their comments.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0194\n\n\n\nRules of interpretation\n\n\n\nAny arbitration panel shall interpret the provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173 in accordance with customary rules of interpretation of public international law, including those codified in the\u00a0Vienna Convention of 1969 on the Law of Treaties. The arbitration panel shall also take into account relevant interpretations of WTO panels and of the Appellate Body adopted by the WTO Dispute Settlement Body (hereinafter referred to as the \u201cDSB\u201d). The reports of the arbitration panel cannot add to or diminish the rights and obligations of the Parties under this Agreement.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0195\n\n\n\n\n\nDecisions and reports of the arbitration panel\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The deliberations of the arbitration panel shall be confidential. The arbitration panel shall make every effort to take any decision by consensus. Nevertheless, where a decision cannot be arrived at by consensus, the matter at issue shall be decided by majority vote. In no case shall dissenting opinions of arbitrators be disclosed.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The reports of the arbitration panel shall be drafted without the presence of the Parties. The reports shall set out the findings of fact, the applicability of the relevant provisions referred to in Article\u00a0173, and the basic rationale behind any findings and conclusions that it makes.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The reports of the arbitration panel shall be unconditionally accepted by the Parties. They shall not create any rights or obligations for natural or legal persons.\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Parties shall make the arbitration panel report publicly available, subject to the protection of confidential information as provided for in the Rules of Procedure set out in Annex V.\n\n\n\nSECTION\u00a04\n\n\n\nGENERAL PROVISIONS\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0196\n\n\n\nLists of arbitrators\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Cooperation Committee, on the basis of proposals made by the Parties, shall, no later than six months after the entry into force of this Agreement, establish a list of at least\u00a015 individuals who are willing and able to serve as arbitrators. The list shall be composed of three sublists: one sublist for each Party and one sublist of individuals who are not nationals of either Party and who may serve as chairperson of the arbitration panel. Each sublist shall include at least five individuals. The Cooperation Committee will ensure that the list is always maintained at that level.\n\n\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Arbitrators shall have specialised knowledge and experience of law and international trade. They shall be independent, serve in their individual capacities and not take instructions from any organisation or government, or be affiliated with the government of any of the Parties, and shall comply with the Code of Conduct set out in Annex VI.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0The Cooperation Committee may establish additional lists of\u00a015 individuals with knowledge and experience in specific sectors covered by this Agreement. Subject to the agreement of the Parties, such additional lists shall be used to compose the arbitration panel in accordance with the procedure set out in Article\u00a0177.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0197\n\n\n\nRelation with WTO obligations\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Recourse to the dispute settlement provisions of this Title shall be without prejudice to any action in the WTO framework, including dispute settlement action.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0However, a Party shall not, for a particular measure, seek redress for the breach of a substantially equivalent obligation under both this Agreement and the WTO Agreement in both fora. In such a case, once a dispute settlement proceeding has been initiated, the Party shall not bring a claim seeking redress for the breach of the substantially equivalent obligation under the other agreement to the other forum, unless the forum first selected fails for procedural or jurisdictional reasons to make findings on the claim seeking redress of that obligation.\n\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For the purposes of this Article:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0dispute settlement proceedings under the WTO Agreement are deemed to be initiated by a Party\u2019s request for the establishment of a panel under Article\u00a06 of the WTO Understanding on Rules and Procedures Governing the Settlement of Disputes;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0dispute settlement proceedings under this Chapter are deemed to be initiated by a Party\u2019s request for the establishment of an arbitration panel under Article\u00a0176(1).\n\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Nothing in this Agreement shall preclude a Party from implementing the suspension of obligations authorised by the DSB. The WTO Agreement shall not be invoked to preclude a Party from applying temporary remedies for noncompliance under this Chapter.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0198\n\n\n\n\n\nTime limits\n\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0All time limits laid down in this Chapter, including the limits for the arbitration panels to deliver their reports, shall be counted in calendar days, the first day being the day following the act or the fact to which they refer, unless otherwise specified.\n\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Any time limit referred to in this Chapter may be modified by mutual agreement of the Parties to the dispute. The arbitration panel may at any time propose to the Parties to modify any time limit referred to in this Chapter, stating the reasons for that proposal.\n\n\n\nTITLE IV\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF ECONOMIC \nAND SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a01\n\n\n\nECONOMIC DIALOGUE\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0199\n\n\n\nThe Parties adhere to the principles of the free market economy ensuring sound macroeconomic policies and shall develop and strengthen regular economic dialogue aimed at further expanding and deepening mutually beneficial economic ties, as well as sustainable development and economic growth.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0200\n\n\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall regularly review the status of bilateral cooperation and conduct regular exchange of information, expertise and best practices in the field of economic policies, economic and financial development and statistics.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a02\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN PUBLIC FINANCE MANAGEMENT, \nINCLUDING PUBLIC AUDIT AND INTERNAL CONTROL\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0201\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall cooperate in the area of public finance management, including public audit and internal control, with the aim of further development of a sound public finance management system, compatible with the principles of economy, efficiency and effectiveness as well as transparency and accountability.\n\n\n\nCooperation shall include:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promoting the implementation of acceptable and generally recognised international standards as well as convergence with good practices of the European Union in this area;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of information and experiences in this area.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a03\n\n\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF TAXATION\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0202\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall strive to improve international cooperation in the area of taxation, notably in the area of facilitating the collection of legitimate tax revenues, and to develop measures in line with international standards for the effective implementation of the principles of good governance in the area of taxation, including transparency and exchange of information. The Parties shall strengthen dialogue and exchange experience with a view to avoiding harmful tax practices.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a04\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF STATISTICS\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0203\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall promote the harmonisation of statistical methods and practice, including the gathering and dissemination of statistics. The statistical cooperation shall focus on exchange of knowledge, fostering good practices and respect for the UN Fundamental Principles of Official Statistics and the European Statistics Code of Practice.\n\n\n\nThe European Union shall contribute to this end by rendering technical assistance to the Republic of Kazakhstan.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a05\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF ENERGY\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0204\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall continue and intensify their current cooperation on energy matters with the objective to enhance energy security, efficiency, sustainability, and competitiveness. The cooperation shall be based on a comprehensive partnership and shall be guided by the principles of mutual interest, reciprocity, transparency and predictability according to the principles of market economy and existing related multilateral and bilateral agreements.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0205\n\n\n\nCooperation shall include, inter alia, the following areas:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0implementation of energy strategies and policies, elaboration of forecasts and scenarios, including global market conditions for energy products, as well as improvement of the statistical system in the energy sector;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0creation of an attractive and stable investment climate and the encouragement of mutual investments in the energy field on a nondiscriminatory and transparent basis;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0effective cooperation with the European Investment Bank, the European Bank for Reconstruction and Development and other international financial institutions and instruments to support the energy cooperation between the Parties;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0enhancement of scientific and technical cooperation and exchange of information for the development of energy technologies with particular attention to energy efficient and environmentally friendly technologies, in accordance with Chapter\u00a03 (Cooperation in Research and Innovation) of Title VI;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0management and technical training in the energy sector through, inter alia, facilitating exchange of trainees of specialised courses in higher education institutes in the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan as well as development of joint training programmes in accordance with good practices;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0extension of cooperation in multilateral energy fora, initiatives and institutions;\n\n\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0cooperation in exchange of knowledge and experience as well as technology transfer in innovation, including in the areas of management and energy technologies.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0206\n\n\n\nHydrocarbon energy\n\n\n\nCooperation in the field of hydrocarbon energy shall cover the following areas:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0modernisation and enhancement of existing, and development of future, energy infrastructures of common interest according to market principles, including those aimed at diversification of energy sources, suppliers and transportation routes and transport methods, as well the establishment of new generation capacity and the integrity, efficiency, safety and security of energy infrastructures, including electric power infrastructures;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0development of competitive, transparent and nondiscriminatory energy markets in line with best practices through regulatory reforms;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0enhancement and strengthening of longterm stability and security of energy trade, including ensuring the predictability and stability of energy demand, on a nondiscriminatory basis, while minimising environmental impacts and risks;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promotion of a high level of environmental protection and sustainable development in the energy sector, including extraction, production, distribution and consumption;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0strengthening the safety of offshore hydrocarbon exploration and production activities, by means of exchange of experience in accident prevention, postaccident analysis, response and remediation policies, as well as best practices on liability and legal practice in case of a disaster.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0207\n\n\n\n\n\nRenewable energy sources\n\n\n\nCooperation shall be pursued in the fields of:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the development of renewable energy sources in an economic and environmentally sound manner, including cooperation on regulatory issues, certification and standardisation as well as on technological development;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0facilitating exchanges between the Republic of Kazakhstan and European institutions, laboratories and private sector entities, including through joint programmes, with the aim of implementing best practices towards creating the energy of the future and green economy;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0conducting joint seminars, conferences and training programmes, and exchanging information and open statistical data on a regular basis, as well as information on the development of renewable energy sources.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0208\n\n\n\nEnergy efficiency and energy savings\n\n\n\nCooperation in the promotion of energy efficiency and energy savings, including in the coal sector, gas flaring (and the use of associated gas), buildings, appliances and transport, shall be pursued, inter alia, through:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchanging information about energy efficiency policies and legal and regulatory frameworks and action plans;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0facilitating the exchange of experiences and knowhow in the field of energy efficiency and energy savings;\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0initiating and implementing projects, including demonstration projects, for the introduction of innovative technologies and solutions in the field of energy efficiency and energy savings;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0training programmes and training courses in the field of energy efficiency in order to achieve the objectives of this Article.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a06\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF TRANSPORT\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0209\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall cooperate on:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0expanding and strengthening their transport cooperation in order to contribute to the development of sustainable transport systems;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0focusing on the social and environmental aspects of the transport systems;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promoting efficient, safe and secure transport operations;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0enhancing the main transport links between their territories.\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0210\n\n\n\nThe cooperation referred to in this Chapter shall cover, among others, the following areas:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of best practices on transport policies;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0improvement of the movement of passengers and goods, increasing fluidity of transport flows by removing administrative, technical and other obstacles, aiming at closer market integration, improving transport networks and upgrading the infrastructure;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0information exchange and joint activities at regional and international level and implementation of applicable international agreements and conventions;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of best practices on\u00a0safety and sustainable development of\u00a0maritime transport.\n\n\n\nThe Republic of Kazakhstan shall bring its bilateral aviation agreements with the Member\u00a0States of the European Union in accordance with the legislation of the European Union.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0211\n\n\n\nA regular dialogue shall take place on the issues covered by this Chapter.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a07\n\n\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF ENVIRONMENT\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0212\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall develop and strengthen their cooperation on environmental issues, thereby contributing to sustainable development and good governance in environmental protection.\n\n\n\nCooperation shall be pursued in the following fields:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0environmental assessments, monitoring and control;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0environmental education and awareness raising, improving access to information, enhancing public participation in decision making and access to justice in environmental matters;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0legislation in the field of environmental protection;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0air quality;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0waste management;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0water quality management, including marine environment;\n\n\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0integrated water resource management, including promotion of advanced water saving technologies;\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0conservation and protection of biological and landscape diversity;\n\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0sustainable forest management;\n\n\n\n(j)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0industrial pollution and industrial emissions;\n\n\n\n(k)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0classification and safe management of chemicals;\n\n\n\n(l)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0initiatives of the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan in the area of green economy; and\n\n\n\n(m)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0mutual exchange of experience regarding the policies for sustainable development of fisheries.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0213\n\n\n\nCooperation in the field of environmental protection shall be carried out by mutual consent of the Parties in, among others, the following forms:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of technologies, scientific and technical information, and research activities in the field of environmental protection;\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of experience in improvement of environmental legislation and methodologies.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0214\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall pay special attention to the implementation of, and cooperation in, environmental issues in the framework of relevant multilateral environmental agreements and agree to intensify cooperation at regional level.\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall exchange experience in promoting integration of the environment into other sectors, including exchanging best practices, increasing knowledge and competence, environmental education and awareness raising in the areas referred to in this Chapter.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a08\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF CLIMATE CHANGE\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0215\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall develop and strengthen their cooperation to combat and to adapt to climate change. Cooperation shall be conducted considering the interests of the Parties on the basis of equality and mutual benefit and taking into account the interdependence existing between bilateral and multilateral commitments in this field.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0216\n\n\n\nCooperation shall promote measures at domestic and international level, including in the following areas:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0mitigation of climate change;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0adaptation to climate change;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0market and nonmarket approaches to addressing climate change;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0research, development, demonstration, deployment and diffusion of new, safe and sustainable lowcarbon and adaptation technologies;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of climate expertise and support for other sectors;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0awareness raising, education and training.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0217\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall, inter alia, exchange information and expertise, implement joint research activities and exchanges of information on cleaner technologies, implement joint activities at regional and international level, including with regard to multilateral environmental agreements applicable to the Parties, such as the UN Framework Convention on Climate Change, and joint activities in the framework of relevant agencies, as appropriate.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a09\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF INDUSTRY\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0218\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall develop and strengthen their cooperation on industry, including issues of development of effective incentives and favourable conditions for the further diversification and an increase in competitiveness of the manufacturing industry.\n\n\n\nTo that end, the Parties shall cooperate, including through the exchange of best practices and experience, in the following sectors:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0productivity and efficiency of resource use;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0public supporting measures for industry sectors, based on WTO requirements and other applicable rules of the Parties;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0implementation of the industrial policy within a context of deepening integration;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0tools to enhance the efficiency of the implementation of industrial policy;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0investment activity in the manufacturing industry, reduction of its energy consumption, as well as the exchange of experiences in the implementation of labour productivity policies;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0conditions for the development of new production technologies, hightech industries, and knowledge and technology transfer, as well as further development of basic infrastructure and favourable environment for innovation clusters;\n\n\n\n(g)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0investment and trade in mining and production of raw materials, with the objectives of promoting mutual understanding and transparency, improving the business environment, and promoting the exchange of information and cooperation in the area of nonenergy mining, in particular metallic ores and industrial minerals;\n\n\n\n(h)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0human resource capacity development in the manufacturing industry;\n\n\n\n\n\n(i)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promotion of business initiatives and industrial cooperation between enterprises of the European Union and the Republic of Kazakhstan.\n\n\n\nThis Agreement does not exclude greater industrial cooperation between the Parties, and separate arrangements may be concluded.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a010\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF SMALL AND MEDIUMSIZED ENTERPRISES\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0219\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall develop and strengthen their cooperation in the area of small and mediumsized enterprises (SMEs) to foster a business environment conducive to the successful development and creation of SMEs.\n\n\n\nTo that end, the Parties shall cooperate in the following fields:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of information on SME development policy;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of best practices on initiatives strengthening entrepreneurship as a key competence;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promotion of better contacts between business associations of both Parties through closer dialogue;\n\n\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of experience in supporting the capacity of SMEs to access international markets;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of experience in the area of improving the regulatory framework impact on SMEs;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of best practices on access to financing for SMEs.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a011\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF COMPANY LAW\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0220\n\n\n\nThe Parties recognise the importance of an effective set of rules and practices in the areas of company law and corporate governance, as well as in accounting and auditing, in a functioning market economy with a predictable and transparent business environment, and underline the importance of promoting regulatory convergence in this field.\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall cooperate on the following:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of best practices on ensuring availability of and access to information regarding the organisation and representation of registered companies in a transparent and easily accessible way;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0further development of corporate governance policy in line with international and particularly OECD standards;\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0fostering the implementation and consistent application of International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS) for the consolidated accounts of listed companies;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the approximation of accounting rules and financial reporting, including as regards SMEs;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the regulation and oversight of the auditor and accountant professions;\n\n\n\n(f)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0international auditing standards and the Code of Ethics of the International Federation of Accountants (IFAC), with the aim of improving the professional level of auditors by means of observance of standards and ethical norms by professional organisations, audit organisations and auditors.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a012\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF BANKING, INSURANCE \nAND OTHER FINANCIAL SERVICES\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0221\n\n\n\nThe Parties agree on the importance of effective legislation and practices and to cooperate in the area of financial services with the objectives of:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0improving the regulation of financial services;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensuring effective and adequate protection of investors and consumers of financial services;\n\n\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0contributing to the stability and integrity of the global financial system;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promoting cooperation between different actors of the financial system, including regulators and supervisors;\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promoting independent and effective supervision.\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall promote regulatory convergence with recognised international standards for sound financial systems.\n\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a013\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF INFORMATION SOCIETY\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0222\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall promote cooperation on the development of the information society to benefit citizens and businesses through the widespread availability of information and communication technologies (ICT) and through better quality of services at affordable prices. This cooperation shall aim at promoting the development of competition in, and openness of, ICT markets as well as encouraging investments in this sector.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0223\n\n\n\nCooperation shall cover, inter alia, exchange of information and best practices on the implementation of information society initiatives, focusing notably on:\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0developing an effective regulatory framework for the ICT sector;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promoting broadband access;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0developing interoperable electronic services;\n\n\n\n(d)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0ensuring data protection; and\n\n\n\n(e)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0developing roaming services.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0224\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall promote cooperation between the regulators in the field of ICT, including electronic communications, in the the European Union and Republic of Kazakhstan.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER\u00a014\n\n\n\nCOOPERATION IN THE AREA OF TOURISM\n\n\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0225\n\n\n\nThe Parties shall cooperate in the field of tourism with the aim of strengthening the development of a competitive and sustainable tourism industry as a generator of economic growth, empowerment, employment and exchanges in the tourism sector.\n\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0226\n\n\n\nCooperation shall be based on the following principles:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0respect for the integrity and interests of local communities, particularly in rural areas;\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0the importance of preserving cultural and historical heritage; and\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0positive interaction between tourism and environmental preservation.\n\n\n\nARTICLE\u00a0227\n\n\n\nCooperation shall focus on the following topics:\n\n\n\n(a)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0exchange of information, best practices, experience and knowhow, including on innovative technologies;\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0establishment of a strategic partnership between public, private and community stakeholders in order to support the sustainable development of tourism;\n\n\n\n(c)\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0promotion and development of tourism
